Al-Ijma — Consensus

7 min
Two Additional Proofs for Khabar al-Wahid: Ijma' and Rational Necessity
Presents ijma' and rational argument for authority of single-narrator reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ijma' and aqli (rational) arguments for the authority of khabar al-wahid and explain how they complement the primary textual proofs.

Core Idea
The Companions' consensus and the necessity of avoiding legal suspension prove khabar al-wahid is a binding source.

In this passage, the author expands on the proofs for the authority of khabar al-wahid by presenting two additional arguments beyond the Quran and Sunnah. First, the ijma' (consensus) of the Companions, who themselves used single-narrator reports without any expression of rejection. Second, a rational argument: since mutawatir and mashhur reports are not available for every incident, rejecting khabar al-wahid would lead to the suspension of many rulings. This lesson unpacks both proofs and shows how they strengthen the Hanafi position on khabar al-wahid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the additional proofs
The text presents two proofs beyond Quran and Sunnah: ijma' and ma'qul (rational).
2
Examine the ijma' argument
The Companions themselves argued using khabar al-wahid, as shown by Abu Bakr's argument about Quraysh and their acceptance without denial.
3
Understand the scope of ijma'
The Companions also agreed on accepting khabar al-wahid in matters of water purity/impurity, showing comprehensive application.
4
Analyze the rational argument
Since mutawatir and mashhur narrations are not available for every incident, rejecting khabar al-wahid would lead to suspension of many rulings. This necessity proves its authority.
5
Synthesize the proofs
These arguments place khabar al-wahid on firm ground: textual (Quran/Sunnah), consensual (ijma'), and rational (ma'qul).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَقَعَ فِي بَعْضِ النُّسَخِ قَوْلُهُ وَالإجْمَاعُ وَالمَعْقُولُ عَطْفًا عَلَى الكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ فَالإجْمَاعُ هُوَ أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ احْتَجُّوا بِأَخْبَارِ الآحَادِ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمْ وَاحْتَجَّ أَبُو بَكْرٍ عَلَى الأَنْصَارِ بِقَوْلِهِ الأَئِمَّةُ مِنْ قُرَيْشٍ فَقَبِلُوا مِنْ غَيْرِ نَكِيرٍ وَهَكَذَا أَجْمَعُوا عَلَى قُبُولِ خَبَرِ الأَحَادِ فِي طَهَارَةِ المَاءِ وَنَجَاسَتِهِ وَالمَعْقُولُ هُوَ أَنَّ المُتَوَاتِرَ وَالمَشْهُورَ لَا يُوجَدَانِ فِي كُلِّ حَادِثَةٍ فَلَوْ رُدَّ خَبَرُ الْوَاحِدِ فِيهَا لَتَعَطَّلَتِ الأَحْكَامُ
And it occurs in some copies: 'and consensus and the rational' as an apposition to 'the Book and the Sunnah'. So consensus is that the Companions argued with single-narrator reports among themselves, and Abu Bakr argued against the Ansar with his saying 'the rulers are from Quraysh', and they accepted without denial. Likewise, they agreed upon accepting single-narrator reports concerning the purity and impurity of water. And the rational is that the mutawatir and the mashhur are not found in every incident; so if the single-narrator report were rejected therein, the rulings would be suspended.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage provides additional proofs for the authority of khabar al-wahid beyond the primary textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The author presents two arguments: first, ijma' (consensus) of the Companions, who used khabar al-wahid in their deliberations, exemplified by Abu Bakr's argument for Quraysh leadership and their unanimous acceptance of such reports in matters of water purity. Second, a rational argument: mutawatir and mashhur reports are not available for every incident; if khabar al-wahid were rejected, many legal rulings would be left without evidence, leading to their suspension. This demonstrates that khabar al-wahid is necessary for deriving rulings in the absence of higher categories of reports.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the Companions on accepting khabar al-wahid as proof.
المعقول (al-ma'qul): Rational argument showing the necessity of khabar al-wahid due to lack of tawatur in every case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what rational argument supports the authority of khabar al-wahid?
A) The Quran explicitly commands following khabar al-wahid.
B) Mutawatir and mashhur reports are not available in every incident, so rejecting khabar al-wahid would leave rulings suspended.
C) The Sunnah contains many single-narrator reports.
D) The Companions never disagreed about khabar al-wahid.

Key Takeaway
Ijma' of the Companions and rational necessity together confirm that khabar al-wahid is a binding source for deriving rulings.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

Conditions for Accepting News in Mixed Obligation Cases
Ruling on conditions for accepting news involving obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in news with mixed obligation (min wajh al-ilzam), half the testimony conditions are required, and evaluate the Sahibayn's alternative position.

Core Idea
When a report involves both obligation and non-obligation, the Hanafi school requires half the testimony: either two witnesses or one just witness.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar examines a nuanced usul rule: the conditions for accepting a report (khabar) depend on the degree of obligation (ilzam) present in the matter. The author distinguishes three scenarios—no obligation, pure obligation, and mixed obligation—and presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Understanding this rule helps us determine when a single just witness suffices versus full testimony conditions.

Guided Path
1
Classify the type of news by obligation
Determine whether the news imposes obligations (ilzam) on the recipient. The passage identifies three types: no ilzam (like gift news), pure ilzam (like testimony in court), and mixed ilzam (like news of a wakil's dismissal).
The distinction hinges on whether the news creates a legal duty or only permits a beneficial act.
2
Recall the default rules for pure and no ilzam
For no ilzam, no condition, any reporter suffices. For pure ilzam, full testimony: both number (two witnesses) and justice are required. This is the baseline.
The Prophet's acceptance of gift news from righteous and sinful people supports the no-condition rule.
3
Analyze the mixed case: Abu Hanifa's reasoning
In mixed ilzam, Abu Hanifa balances both aspects: he requires only one half of testimony conditions—either the number (two reporters) or the justice of the reporter (one just witness). This ensures neither aspect is entirely ignored.
The ruling text says 'we have given full consideration to both sides'.
4
Contrast with the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require no conditions at all for mixed news; any discerning person suffices. They prioritize the non-obligation aspect, considering that the news itself does not create a legal obligation.
The practical difference: a fasiq reporter would be accepted by Sahibayn but not by Abu Hanifa.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical outcome: in cases like news of a wakil's dismissal by a sinful intermediary, Abu Hanifa rejects it (unless the reporter is two people or a just witness), while Sahibayn accept it. This affects daily transactions.
The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's according to the later Hanafi tradition, but the passage does not explicitly tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں (بچہ) ہو یا بالغ یا آزادی غلام اور مسلمان ہویا کافر عادل ہو یا ناسق ہو۔ پس جس کو خبر دی گئی ہے اس کے لئے وکالت کرنا، مال میں شرکت کرنا اور اس میں تصرف کرنا اور اس کے مطابق عمل درآمد کر ناصریح ہے، کیونکہ انسان بہت ہی کم ایسا آدمی پائے گا جو تمام صفات کا جامع ہو جسے دور کیل کے پاس بھیجے لہذا اگر مذکورہ شرطیں یہاں بھی ضروری قرار دی جائیں گی تو عالم سے مصالح معطل ہو کر رہ جائیں گی۔ نیز دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ نفس خبر کسی چیز کو واقع میں لازم نہیں کرتی۔ لہذا الزام کی شرائط کا اس میں کیسے اعتبار کیا جائے گا نیز نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہدیہ کی خبر صالح وفاجر ہر ایک کی قبول فرما لیتے تھے۔
وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيْهِ انا الح اور اگر محل خیر ایسی ہو کہ جس میں من وجه الزام ہو اور من وجه الزام نہ ہو جیسے وکیل کے معزول کرنے کی خبر اور عمید مازون کو مجور قرار دیئے جانے کی خبر ۔ تو اس حیثیت سے کہ مؤکل اور مولی اپنے اپنے حقوق میں معد دل کرنے یا مجبور کرنے کا تصرف کرتے ہیں جس طرح وہ وکیل بنانے اور غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دینے کا تصرف کرتے ہیں، اور اس میں کوئی الزام نہیں ہے اور دوسری حیثیت یہ ہے کہ تصرف کا تعلق وکیل سے اور اجازت کے ختم کرنے کا تعلق فلام سے ہے اور اس میں ایک قسم کی ذمہ داری ماکہ ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں وکیل اور عید پر الزام نقصان پایا جاتا ہے۔
فَلِهَذَا يُشْتَرَطَ فِيْهِ أَحَدٌ شطري الشهادة : تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک (نصاب) شہادت کا نصف شرط ہو گا۔ یعنی خواہ عد د پایا جائے۔ یا عدالت پائی جائے یعنی مخبر کا رو ہونا ضروری ہے یا ایک گواہ ہو عادل ہو، دونوں جانب کا لحاظ ر کھتے ہوئے یہ حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ محل خبر اگر الزام محض ہو تو اس میں دونوں چیزیں شرط ہیں۔ عدد بھی اور عدالت بھی اور اگر بالکل الزام نہ ہو تو ان دونوں شرطوں میں سے کسی شرط کی ضرورت نہیں۔ فَوَفِّرْنَا حَظًّا مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنَ لہذا اس میں ہم نے دونوں جانب کی پوری رعایت رکھی ہے۔ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يَسْتَرِطُ فيه شي :- اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس میں کوئی شرط ہی نہیں ہے بلکہ مجور نے معزول کرنے کی خبر ہر تمیز رکھنے والے آدمی کی مقبول ہوگی۔ یہ اس وقت ہے کہ جب مخبر فضولی ہو۔ لیکن اگر خبر دینے والا وکیل ہو یا موکل اور مولی کا بھیجا ہوا قاصد ہو ۔ تو بالاتفاق عدد اور عدالت کی کوئی شرط نہیں ہے۔
Whether (the reporter) is a child or adult, free or slave, Muslim or disbeliever, just or sinful. Then for the person who is given the news, it is permissible to appoint (him as) a deputy, to share in property, to transact in it, and to act upon it accordingly, because a person will rarely find someone who combines all attributes such that he sends him to a distant place. So if these conditions were made necessary here, then the public interests would be left unattended. Also, the second point is that the news itself does not necessitate something in reality. So how can the conditions of obligation be considered in it? Also, the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to accept the news of a gift from both the righteous and the sinful. And if the locus of the news is such that it has obligation from one aspect and no obligation from another, like the news of dismissing a deputy and the news of appointing a slave as authorized [ma'dhun] — from the perspective that the principal and master are making the dismissal or appointment by their own disposition just as they make the appointment and permission for trade, and there is no obligation in that; and from the other perspective, the disposition relates to the deputy and the termination of permission relates to the slave, and in that there is a kind of responsibility, so in that case there is found the imposition of harm on the deputy and slave. Therefore, in this case one of the two halves of testimony is required: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, half of the testimony requirement — i.e., either number (two witnesses) or justice (the reporter must be two persons or a single just witness), considering both sides, this ruling is given. Because if the locus of the news is pure obligation, both conditions are required: number and justice. And if there is no obligation at all, then none of these two conditions are needed. Thus we have given full consideration to both sides. And according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), no condition is required in this; rather, the news of dismissal or appointment from every discerning person is acceptable. This is when the reporter is a third party. But if the reporter is the deputy himself or a messenger sent by the principal or master, then by consensus there is no condition of number or justice.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage addresses the conditions for accepting a report (khabar) from a single person (khabar al-wahid) in matters that involve some degree of obligation (ilzam). The discussion arises from a previous context about general permission to act on news from any person regardless of moral character. The author distinguishes three scenarios: (1) where the news imposes no obligation at all (e.g., news of a gift or a beneficial transaction) — here no conditions are needed, and even a child or sinner's report is acceptable; (2) where the news is purely obligatory (ilzam mahd) — then full testimony conditions (two witnesses or one just witness) are required; (3) where the news has both aspects (min wajh al-ilzam wa min wajh la ilzam), like news of a deputy's dismissal or a slave's appointment as authorized — here Imam Abu Hanifa requires half the testimony: either two witnesses (number) or one just witness (justice), considering both sides. The two companions (Sahibayn) require nothing in this case, arguing that the reporter's discernment suffices. However, if the reporter is the deputy himself or the principal's messenger, all agree there is no condition because their statement is like that of the principal himself.

Key Terms
خبر واحد (khabar al-wahid): A report from a single person that is not mutawatir
الزام (ilzam): Imposition of an obligation or legal liability on someone
شطر الشهادة (shatr al-shahada): One of the two requirements of testimony (either number or justice)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is required when the news involves both obligation and non-obligation (min wajh al-ilzam)?
A) Both number and justice (two just witnesses)
B) Only one condition: either two witnesses or one just witness
C) No condition at all; any discerning person suffices
D) The reporter must be a wakil or messenger

Key Takeaway
The condition for accepting news in mixed obligation cases is half the testimony requirements: either two witnesses or one just witness.

Effect of Narrator Denial and Contradiction on Hadith
Ruling on narrator denial/contradiction in hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify narrator behaviors (definitive denial, hesitant denial, contradictory action) and apply the Hanafi principle to determine whether the hadith can be acted upon.

Core Idea
Definitive denial drops the hadith by consensus; hesitant denial splits the scholars; clear contradictory action after narration also drops it.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational rule in Hanafi usul: how does a narrator's denial or contradictory action affect the reliability of a hadith? The passage presents a clear taxonomy: outright denial, hesitant denial, and post-narration contradiction. It also addresses nuances like timing and multiple interpretations. Understanding this taxonomy is crucial for evaluating the strength of transmitted reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of narrator behavior
Scan the passage and identify whether the narrator's action is a denial (inkar) or a contradictory act (amal bi khilaf). For denial, note if it is definitive (jahid) or hesitant (mutawaqqif).
The passage explicitly categorizes three scenarios.
2
Determine the ruling for definitive denial
If the narrator says 'you lied' or 'I never narrated this', the hadith is dropped by consensus (ittifaq). Understand why: the denial is certain and undermines the chain.
This is the only case with full consensus.
3
Analyse hesitant denial
When the narrator says 'I don't remember' or 'I don't know', there is ikhtilaf. The Hanafi imam al-Karkhi and Ahmad ibn Hanbal drop it; Shafi'i and Malik do not. Consider the logical basis for each.
The Hanafi school has no single ruling; both views appear in texts.
4
Examine contradictory action after narration
If the narrator acts contrary to the hadith after narrating it, and the contradiction is certain (bi-yaqin), the hadith is dropped. The reason is either the narrator knew of abrogation/fabrication (dropping the hadith as evidence) or acted negligently (dropping his integrity).
Timing matters: action before narration or unknown date is not a defect.
5
Distinguish specification of interpretation
If the narrator simply interprets the hadith in one of multiple possible ways and acts on that interpretation, it does not prevent acting on other interpretations. Example: Ibn Umar's interpretation of 'separation' in the sale option hadith.
This shows that acting on one plausible meaning is not necessarily a contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ بَيَانِ الْتُقْسِيْمَاتِ الأَرْبَعِ شَرَعَ فِى بَيَانِ طَعْنِ يَلْحَقِّ الْحَدِيْثِ مِنْ جانب الزاوئ أَوْ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ فَقَالَ وَالْمَرْوِئ عَنْهُ إِذَا انْكَرَ الرّوَايَةَ فَإِنْ كَانَ إنْكَار جَاهِدٌ بأن يَقُولَ كَذَبْتَ على وَمَا رَوَيْتُ لَكَ هَذا يَسقط العَمَلُ بِالْحَدِيْثِ الْفَاقًا وَإِنْ كَانَ إِنْكَارُ مُتَوَقِّف بِأَنْ يَقُولَ لَا أَذْكُرُ أَنِّى رَوَيْتَ لَكَ هَذَا الْحَدِيْثِ أَوْ لَا أَعْرِفة فَفِيْهِ خِلافٌ فَعِنْدَ الْكَرْخِي وَأَحْمَدَ بْنِ حَنْبَلٍ يَسْقُطُ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ وَعِنْدَ الشافعي ومالك لا يسقط أوْ عَمِلَ بِخِلافِهِ بَعْدَ الرَّوَايَةِ مِمَّا هُوَ خَلافٌ بَيَقِيْنِ سَقَطَ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ لأنَّه إن خَالَفَة لِلوقوفِ عَلَى نَسبْخِهِ أَوْ مَوْضُوعِيتِهِ فَقَط سَقَط الاحتجاج به وان خَالَفَ لِقِلْةِ الْمُبالاة به أَوْ لِغَفْلَتِهِ فَقَدْ سَقَطَتْ عَدَالله مِثَالُهُ مَارُوتَ عَائِشَة أَنَّهُ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَيُّمَا امْرَأَةٍ نَكَحَتْ بِلا إِذْنِ وَلِيْهَا فَنِكَاحُها بَاطِلٌ ثُمَّ أَنْهَا زَوْجَتُ بنت اختها بلا إذْنِ وَلِيْهَا وَإِنْمَا قَالَ خِلافٌ بَيَقِيْنِ إِحْتِرَارًا عَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ مُحْتَمِلاً للْمَعْتَتِيْنِ فَعَمَلَ بِأحَدِهِمَا عَلى مَا سَيَاتِي وَإِنْ كَانَ قَبْلَ الرِّوَايَةِ أَوْ لَمْ يَعْرِفْ تَارِيخ لَمْ يَكُن جَرْحًا أَمَّا عَلَى الأَوْلِ فَلانَ الظَّاهِرَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ مَذْهَبَة فَتَرَكَةَ لأَجَلٍ الْحَدِيْثِ وَأَمَّا عَلَى الثَّانِي فَلانَ الْحَدِيثُ حُجةٌ بِأَصْلِهِ وَوَقَوْعِ السَّنَكِ فِى سقوطه لجمل التاريخ لَايُسْقِطَة قَط وَتَعْيِييْن الرَّاوِئ بَعْضَ مُحْتِمَلاتِهِ بِأَنْ كَانَ مُسْتَرِكًا لعَمَل يَتَاوِيلِ مِنْهُ لاَ يَمْنَعُ الْعَمَلَ بِهِ لِلتَّاوِيلِ الآخَرِ كَمَا رُوِيَ بْنَ عُمَرَ أَنَّهُ قَالَ الْمُتَبَايَعَانِ المتبايعان بِالْخِيَارِ مَالَمْ يَتَفَرقَا فَهَذَا يَحْتَمِلُ تَفَرَّقَ الْأَمْوَالِ وَتَفَرُقِ الأَبْدَانِ وَأَوْلَهُ اِبْنَ عُمَرَ الرَّارِئ يَتَفَرُقِ الأَبْدَانِ كَمَا هُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافَعِي وَهَذَا لَا يَنَا فِي أَنْ نَعْمَلْ نَحْنُ بِتَفَرقِ الأَقْوَالِ وَالاِمْتِنَاعُ أَى امْتِنَاعُ الرَّاوِئَ عَنِ الْعَمَلِ بِهِ مِثْلَ الْعَمَلِ بِخَلافِهِ أَنْ بخلافِ مَارَوَاهُ فَيَخْرُجُ عَنِ الْكَمَا رَوَى ابْنُ عُمَر أَنه عَلَيْهِ السَّلام كَانَ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عِنْدَ الرُّكُوعِ وَعِنْدَ رَفْعِ الرَّاسِ مِنَ الرُّكُوعِ وَقَدْ صَعْ عَنِ مُجَاهِدٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ صَحِبْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ عَشْرَ سِنِينَ فَلَمْ أَرَاهُ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ إِلا فِى تَكْبِيرَةِ الافتتاح فتَرْك الْعَمَل بِهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى انْتِسَاخِه.
ترجمہ و تشریح اس عیب کا بیان جو حدیث کو لاحق ہوتا ہے ۔ وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ بَيَانِ التُقْسِبُعَاتِ الْأَرْبَعِ ہے۔ مصنف جب سنت کی چاروں تقسیموں سے فارغ ہو گئے تو انھوں نے اس طعن (عیب ) کا بیان شروع کیا جو حدیث کو راوی کی جانب سے یا اس کے غیر سے لاحق ہوا کرتا ہے۔ تو فرما لو المروى عنه اذا أنكر الروایۃ اور مروی عنہ جب سرے سے روایت کا انکار کر دے پس اگر انکار جامد ہے (یعنی جان بوجھ کر انکار کرنے والا ) بایں طور کہ وہ کہتا ہے تو نے مجھ پر جھوٹ بولا حالا نکہ یہ حدیث میں نے تجھ سے روایت نہیں کی تو اس قسم کا انکار بالا تفاق عمل بالحدیث کو ساقط کر دیتا ہے اور اگر انکار متوقف ہے (یعنی کسی تامل کرنے والے نے انکار کیا ہو ) مزادہ کہتا ہے مجھے یاد نہیں ہے کہ میں نے تم سے یہ حدیث روایت کی ہے یاوہ کہتا ہے کہ میں یہ حدیث نہیں جانتا تو اس میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے امام کرتی اور احمد بن فضیل کے نزدیک اس روایت پر مکمل ساقط ہے اور امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک عمل ساقط نہیں ہو گا۔
أَوْ عَمَلَ بِخِلافِهِ بَعْدَ الرواية- یا روایت حدیث کے بعد روایت کرنے والا اس حدیث کے خلاف عمل کرے اور یہ خلاف پورے یقین کے ساتھ ہو تو دونوں صورتوں میں حدیث پیل کرنا ساقط ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ اگر راد کی نے اس حدیث کے منسوخ ہونے کی واقفیت کی وجہ سے اس حدیث کا خلاف کیا ہے یا اس کے موضوع ہونے کی وجہ سے خلاف کیا ہے تو اس روایت سے حجتہ پکڑنا ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر بے پرواہی کی وجہ سے غفلت کی بنا پر اس کے خلاف عمل کیا ہے تو اس کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اس کی مثال وہ حدیث ہے جس کو حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا نے روایت کیا ہے کہ نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے أَيُّمَا امْرَأَةٍ نَكَحَت بِلا إِذْنِ وَلِيْهَا فَنِكَاحُهَا بَاطِل۔ (جو عورت ولی کی اجازت کے بغیر اپنا نکاح کرے تو وہ نکاح باطل ہے) پھر حضرت عائشہ ہی نے اپنی بیجی کا نکاح اس کے ولی کے بغیر کر دیا وانعا قال خلاف بیقین متن میں مصنف نے خلاف بیقین کہا ہے اس سے احتراز کرتا ہے اس حدیث سے جس میں حدیث دو معنی کا احتمال رکھتی ہو ۔ اور مروی عنہ ایک معنی پر عمل کرتا ہو جیسا کہ اس کا بیان آئندہ آئے گا وانْ كَانَ قَبْلَ الرَّوَايَةِ الحَ اور اگر وہ روایت کرنے سے پہلے وہ اس حدیث کے خلاف عمل کرتا تھا۔ یا اس کے روایت کرنے کی تاریخ ہی معلوم نہ ہو ۔ تو یہ دونوں صورتیں حدیث میں جرح اور طعن کا سبب نہ ہوں گی۔ بہر حال پہلی صورت (یعنی حدیث کے خلاف مل روایت حدیث سے پہلے تھا تو اس وجہ سے ظاہر ہے کہ اولا اس کا مذ ہب تھا بعد میں حدیث کی وجہ سے اس عمل کو ترک کر دیا ہے۔ اور بہر حال دوسری صورت یعنی دادی کا عمل حدیث کے خلاف ہے۔ مگر روایت حدیث کی تاریخ معلوم
And when he finished explaining the four divisions, he began explaining the defect that afflicts the hadith from the side of the narrator or others, and he said: The one from whom the narration is made, when he denies the narration: if the denial is definitive such that he says 'You lied about me, I did not narrate this to you,' then acting upon the hadith is dropped by consensus. If the denial is hesitating such that he says 'I do not remember that I narrated this hadith to you' or 'I do not know it,' then there is disagreement: according to al-Karkhi and Ahmad ibn Hanbal, acting upon it is dropped; according to al-Shafi'i and Malik, it is not dropped. Or if he acts contrary to it after the narration in a way that is clearly contradictory (with certainty), then acting upon it is dropped because if he opposed it due to knowing its abrogation or fabrication, then using it as evidence is dropped; and if he opposed out of carelessness or negligence, then his integrity is dropped. An example is what Aisha narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, her marriage is invalid.' Then she married her brother's daughter without the guardian's permission. And he only said 'clearly contradictory' to avoid the case where the hadith is open to two possible meanings and he acted on one of them, as will come later. If it was before the narration or the date is unknown, it is not a defect. As for the first, because the apparent is that it was his madhhab and he left it for the hadith. As for the second, because the hadith is a proof in itself and the possibility of abrogation occurring is not sufficient to drop it. And the narrator specifying one of its possible meanings, if he acts according to an interpretation of it, does not prevent acting upon it according to the other interpretation, as was narrated from Ibn Umar that he said: 'The two parties to a transaction have the option as long as they have not separated.' This is open to the separation of wealth and separation of bodies, and Ibn Umar, the narrator, interpreted it as separation of bodies, which is the opinion of al-Shafi'i. And this does not prevent us from acting upon separation of speech (verbal separation). And the narrator refraining from acting upon it is like acting contrary to it. So he goes against what he narrated, as Ibn Umar narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to raise his hands at the time of bowing and at raising the head from bowing, but it is transmitted from Mujahid that he said: 'I accompanied Ibn Umar for ten years and I did not see him raise his hands except in the opening takbir.' So leaving to act upon it indicates its abrogation. Translation and explanation: This is the explanation of the defect that afflicts the hadith. 'And when he finished explaining the four divisions' – when the author finished the four divisions of the Sunnah, he began explaining the defect (al-ta'n) that afflicts the hadith from the side of the narrator or others. So he says: al-marwi 'anhu idha ankara al-riwayah – when the one from whom the narration is made denies the narration. So if the denial is definitive (i.e., intentional), like he says 'You lied about me, I did not narrate this hadith to you,' then this denial drops acting upon the hadith by consensus. And if the denial is hesitating (i.e., a hesitant person denies), like he says 'I do not remember that I narrated this hadith to you' or 'I do not know this hadith,' then there is disagreement among the imams. According to Imam al-Karkhi and Ahmad ibn Hanbal, acting upon it is dropped; according to al-Shafi'i and Malik, it is not dropped. Or he acts contrary to it after the narration – i.e., after narrating the hadith, the narrator acts contrary to it, and this opposition is with certainty. Then in both cases, acting upon the hadith is dropped. Because if the narrator opposed it due to knowledge of its abrogation or due to its being fabricated, then using it as evidence is dropped. And if he opposed out of carelessness or negligence, then his integrity is dropped. An example is the hadith narrated by Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, her marriage is invalid.' Then Aisha herself married her brother's daughter without a guardian. He said 'clearly contradictory' to avoid the hadith that is open to two meanings and the narrator acts on one of them, as will be explained later. If it was before the narration – i.e., the narrator used to act contrary to the hadith before narrating it, or the date of his narration is not known – then these two cases are not a cause for jarh (defect) in the hadith. As for the first case, it is apparent that it was his madhhab initially, then he left it for the hadith. As for the second case, because the hadith is a proof in itself and the possibility of abrogation occurring does not drop it at all. And the narrator specifying one of its possible meanings – if he acts according to an interpretation of it – does not prevent acting upon the other interpretation, as was narrated from Ibn Umar that he said: 'The two parties to a transaction have the option as long as they have not separated.' This is open to separation of wealth and separation of bodies. Ibn Umar interpreted it as separation of bodies, which is the opinion of al-Shafi'i. And this does not prevent us from acting upon separation of speech. And refraining from acting upon it – i.e., the narrator refraining from acting upon it is the same as acting contrary to it. So he goes against what he narrated, as Ibn Umar narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to raise his hands at the time of bowing and at raising the head from bowing. And it is transmitted from Mujahid that he said: 'I accompanied Ibn Umar for ten years, and I did not see him raise his hands except in the opening takbir.' So his leaving to act upon it indicates its abrogation.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains the effect of a narrator denying a hadith or acting contrary to it. It is a usul ruling on the authority of transmitted reports. The author first sets the context: after discussing the four types of Sunnah (qawli, fi'li, taqriri, etc.), he now discusses defects in hadith arising from the narrator. The key ruling: If the narrator outright denies having narrated a hadith (saying 'you lied'), the hadith is dropped by consensus. If he hesitates (does not remember), there is a disagreement: the Hanafi imam al-Karkhi and Ahmad ibn Hanbal drop it; Shafi'i and Malik do not. If the narrator acts contrary to the hadith after narrating it, and the opposition is certain (not just possible), then the hadith is dropped. The reason is either the narrator discovered it was abrogated/fabricated (in which case the evidence falls) or he acted negligently (in which case his integrity falls). The text gives the example of Aisha's hadith on marriage without wali; she narrated it but then acted contrary by marrying her niece without a wali. However, the author specifies 'clearly contradictory' to avoid cases where the hadith can have two interpretations. If the narrator acted before narrating or the date is unknown, it is not a defect. The passage also discusses when a narrator specifies one possible meaning (like Ibn Umar interpreting separation in the sale option hadith as physical separation) – that does not prevent others from acting on the other interpretation. Finally, it cites the example of raising hands in prayer: Ibn Umar narrated raising hands but did not act on it himself, indicating abrogation. This is a classic Hanafi usul discussion on the impact of a narrator's actions on the reliability of a hadith.

Key Terms
إنكار جامد (inkar jahid): A definitive denial where the narrator asserts that the narration is false and accuses the transmitter of lying.
إنكار متوقف (inkar mutawaqqif): A hesitant denial where the narrator does not remember or does not recognize the hadith.
خلاف بيقين (khilaf bi-yaqin): A clear contradiction with certainty, where the narrator's action unequivocally opposes the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a narrator says 'I do not remember narrating this hadith', what is the ruling according to al-Karkhi (Hanafi)?
A) The hadith is dropped by consensus.
B) The hadith is dropped because he is a Hanafi.
C) There is disagreement: al-Karkhi and Ahmad drop it; Shafi'i and Malik do not.
D) The hadith is accepted because denial is not absolute.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's definitive denial or clear contradictory action after narration with certainty drops the hadith; hesitant denial causes disagreement among scholars.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Types of Ijma'
Defining Ijma' and its two types with a rebuttal of Shafi'i counterargument on sukuti ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Ijma' linguistically and technically, distinguish between azima and rukhsa, and explain why the Hanafi school accepts sukuti ijma while the Shafi'i does not.

Core Idea
Ijma' is the agreement of righteous mujtahids; silence after deliberation constitutes binding consensus in the Hanafi school.

After completing the discussion on the Sunnah, the author now turns to the third primary source of Islamic law: Ijma' (consensus). This lesson unpacks its linguistic and technical definitions, breaks down its two pillars (azima and rukhsa), and addresses the key intra-madhhab dispute over the validity of silent consensus (sukuti ijma). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate how legal authority is established when texts are ambiguous.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and technical definitions
Read the Arabic carefully: 'al-ijma'' literally means 'agreement.' Technically, it is the agreement of all righteous mujtahids of the Ummah in one era on a Shar'i matter, whether verbal or practical. Note the conditions: mujtahid, righteous, entire era, Shar'i matter.
The term 'mujtahid' here excludes laypeople; only qualified scholars count.
2
Analyze the two pillars: azima vs rukhsa
Azima (resolve) occurs when all mujtahids explicitly agree, either by saying 'we have agreed' or by collectively beginning a practice (e.g., all engaging in mudaraba). Rukhsa (concession) occurs when only some express an opinion or act, and the rest remain silent after a period of reflection (three days or the same session). This latter type is called sukuti ijma'.
The period of 'muddat al-ta'ammul' is defined as three days or the session; this ensures reflection.
3
Understand the Hanafi acceptance of sukuti ijma'
Hanafis accept silent consensus because silence after a reasonable period indicates approval. The principle is that qualified scholars would not remain silent about error; the Prophet said, 'The one who remains silent about the truth is a dumb devil.'
This hadith is the main dalil for the Hanafi position.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i rejected sukuti ijma', citing the story of Ibn Abbas who disagreed with Umar on al-awl but stayed silent due to Umar's awe. The Hanafi response is that the narration is weak and contradicts Umar's known character of seeking truth from others. Companions would not fail to speak the truth where needed.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if some mujtahids speak and others stay silent, Hanafis consider the ruling binding; Shafi'is do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ أَقْسَامِ السُّنَّةِ شَرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ الإِجْمَاعِ فَقَالَ: بَابُ الإِجْمَاعِ. وَهُوَ فِي اللُّغَةِ الِاتِّفَاقُ، وَفِي الشَّرِيعَةِ: اتِّفَاقُ مُجْتَهِدِينَ صَالِحِينَ مِنْ أُمَّةِ مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي عَصْرٍ وَاحِدٍ عَلَى أَمْرٍ قَوْلِيٍّ أَوْ فِعْلِيٍّ. رُكْنُ الإِجْمَاعِ ضَرْبَانِ: عَزِيمَةٌ، وَهُوَ التَّكَلُّمُ مِنْهُمْ بِمَا يُوجِبُ الِاتِّفَاقَ أَنْ يَتَّفِقَ الْكُلُّ عَلَى الْحُكْمِ بِأَنْ يَقُولُوا أَجْمَعْنَا عَلَى هَذَا إِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْءُ مِنْ بَابِ الْقَوْلِ، أَوْ شُرُوعُهُمْ فِي الْفِعْلِ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ بَابِهِ، كَمَا إِذَا شَرَعَ أَهْلُ الِاجْتِهَادِ جَمِيعًا فِي الْمُضَارَبَةِ أَوِ الْمُدَارَعَةِ أَوِ الشَّرِكَةِ كَانَ ذَلِكَ إِجْمَاعًا مِنْهُمْ عَلَى شَرْعِيَّتِهَا. وَرُخْصَةٌ، وَهُوَ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمَ أَوْ يَفْعَلَ الْبَعْضُ دُونَ الْبَعْضِ، أَيِ اتَّفَقَ بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى قَوْلٍ أَوْ فِعْلٍ وَسَكَتَ الْبَاقُونَ مِنْهُمْ وَلَا يَرُدُّونَ عَلَيْهِمْ بَعْدَ مَضَيِّ مُدَّةِ التَّأَمُّلِ، وَهِيَ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ أَوْ مَجْلِسُ الْعِلْمِ. وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا إِجْمَاعًا سُكُوتِيًّا، وَهُوَ مَقْبُولٌ عِنْدَنَا وَفِيهِ خِلَافُ الشَّافِعِيِّ، لِأَنَّ السُّكُوتَ كَمَا يَكُونُ لِلْمُوَافَقَةِ يَكُونُ لِلْمُقَائَلَةِ وَلَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى الرِّضَا كَمَا رُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ خَالَفَ عُمَرَ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْعَوْلِ، فَقِيلَ لَهُ هَلَّا أَظْهَرْتَ حُجَّتَكَ عَلَى عُمَرَ؟ قَالَ كَانَ رَجُلًا مَهِيبًا فَهَيْبَتُهُ مَنَعَتْنِي. وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّ هَذَا غَيْرُ صَحِيحٍ، لِأَنَّ عُمَرَ كَانَ مُسْتَدْعَى لِاسْتِمَاعِ الْحَقِّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ حَتَّى كَانَ يَقُولُ: لَا خَيْرَ فِيكُمْ مَا لَمْ تَقُولُوا، أَوْ لَا خَيْرَ فِي مَا لَمْ أَسْمَعْ. وَكَيْفَ يُظَنُّ فِي حَقِّ الصَّحَابَةِ التَّقْصِيرُ فِي أُمُورِ الدِّينِ وَالسُّكُوتُ عَنِ الْحَقِّ فِي مَوْضِعِ الْحَاجَةِ؟ وَقَدْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: السَّاكِتُ عَنِ الْحَقِّ شَيْطَانٌ أَخْرَسُ.
And when he finished with the divisions of the Sunnah, he began to explain Ijma'. He said: Chapter of Ijma'. It is in language: agreement, and in Sacred Law: agreement of righteous mujtahids of the Ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in one era on a verbal or practical matter. The pillar of Ijma' is of two types: Azima (resolve), which is their speaking what necessitates agreement, that all agree on the ruling by saying 'we have agreed on this' if the matter is verbal, or their commencing the action if it is of that kind, as when all the people of ijtihad begin doing mudaraba, musaqat, or partnership, that is Ijma' from them on its legality. And Rukhsa (concession), which is that some speak or act without others, i.e., some agree on a saying or action and the rest remain silent and do not reject them after the passage of the period of reflection, which is three days or the session of knowledge. This is called Sukuti Ijma' (silent consensus), and it is accepted according to us, and there is a disagreement with al-Shafi'i because silence can be for opposition as well as agreement and does not indicate contentment, as narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he disagreed with Umar on the issue of al-awl, and it was said to him: 'Why did you not present your proof to Umar?' He said: 'He was a man of awe; his awe prevented me.' The answer is that this is not authentic, because Umar would seek to hear the truth from others to the extent that he used to say: 'There is no good in you as long as you do not speak' or 'no good in what I have not heard.' How can deficiency in matters of religion and silence about the truth in a place of need be imagined of the Companions? And the Prophet (peace and peace be upon him) said: 'The one who remains silent about the truth is a dumb devil.'
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage begins a new topic: Ijma' (consensus). After finishing the discussion on the Sunnah, the author introduces the chapter on Ijma'. First, he gives the linguistic definition: agreement. Then the technical definition: the agreement of the righteous mujtahids of the Ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in a single era on a matter pertaining to speech or action. He then explains that the pillar of Ijma' is of two types. The first is 'azima (strong consensus): where all mujtahids explicitly agree either by saying 'We have agreed on this' (if the matter is verbal) or by all jointly commencing a practice (if it is a practical matter). For example, if all mujtahids simultaneously begin engaging in mudaraba (profit-sharing), musaqat (sharecropping), or partnership, that constitutes their consensus on its legitimacy. The second is 'rukhsa' (concession), which is sukuti ijma (silent consensus): where some mujtahids express an opinion or act, and the rest remain silent without objecting after a period of reflection (three days or the same session). This type is accepted in the Hanafi school, but Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed. His reasoning is that silence could be due to fear or disagreement, not necessarily approval. He cites the incident of Ibn Abbas disagreeing with Umar on the issue of al-awl (inheritance recalculation) and not speaking out due to Umar's awe. The Hanafi response is that this narration is weak because Umar was known to actively seek the truth from others, as he said: 'There is no good in you as long as you do not speak' (or 'as long as I do not hear'). How could the Companions neglect to speak the truth when needed? The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The one who remains silent about the truth is a dumb devil.' Thus, the Companions' silence indicates their approval, not fear.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Agreement of all righteous mujtahids of the Ummah in one era on a Shar'i ruling.
إجماع سكوتي (ijmāʿ sukūtī): Some mujtahids give an opinion and the rest remain silent after a period of reflection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on Sukuti Ijma' (silent consensus)?
A) It is accepted as a valid form of Ijma'.
B) It is rejected because silence may indicate fear.
C) It is accepted only if the silent scholars explicitly state their agreement.
D) It is not considered Ijma' at all.

Key Takeaway
Sukuti ijma is accepted by Hanafis because the silence of qualified scholars after deliberation indicates their consent, supported by the hadith prohibiting silence about the truth.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

Definition and Types of Ijma in Hanafi Usul
Defining Ijma, its two types, and defending silent consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Ijma' in Hanafi usul, distinguish between 'Azimat and Rukhsah, and evaluate the Hanafi acceptance of silent consensus as a binding proof.

Core Idea
Ijma' is the agreement of mujtahids in one era; silent consensus is binding because the Companions would not remain silent about falsehood.

In this lesson, we will explore the foundational concept of Ijma' (consensus) as understood by the Hanafi school. We will examine its precise definition, its division into two types – explicit (azimat) and silent (rukhsah) – and the rigorous defense the Hanafis offer for accepting silent consensus as a binding proof. Understanding this will equip you to recognize the authority of consensus in Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of Ijma'
Read the linguistic and technical definition. Note that it specifies 'mujtahids' and 'one era' and includes both verbal and practical matters.
The definition excludes non-mujtahids and previous eras.
2
Distinguish between 'Azimat and Rukhsah
Identify the two types based on the rukn (pillar). 'Azimat requires explicit agreement from all; Rukhsah (silent consensus) involves some remaining silent after a period of reflection.
The period of reflection is three days or a knowledge session.
3
Explore the conditions for silent consensus
Note the requirement that silence occurs after the opportunity to object and after a sufficient period. The absence of known dissent is crucial.
If a qualified mujtahid later objects, the consensus is broken.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i challenge and Hanafi response
Examine the Shafi'i argument that silence could indicate fear or opposition. Study the Hanafi rebuttal using the example of 'Umar and the hadith about silence concerning truth.
The Hanafi response emphasizes that Companions would not remain silent if they disagreed, as silence about truth is blameworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الإِجْمَاعِ وَهُوَ فِي اللُّغَةِ الاتِّفَاقُ وَفِي الشَّرِيعَةِ اتِّفَاقُ مُجْتَهِدِينَ صَالِحِينَ مِنْ أُمَّةِ مُحَمَّدٍ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي عَصْرٍ وَاحِدٍ عَلَى أَمْرٍ قَوْلِيٍّ أَوْ فِعْلِيٍّ. رُكْنُ الإِجْمَاعِ نَوْعَانِ: عَزِيمَةٌ وَهُوَ التَّكَلُّمُ مِنْهُمْ بِمَا يُوجِبُ الِاتِّفَاقَ، أَنْ يَتَّفِقَ الْكُلُّ عَلَى الْحُكْمِ بِأَنْ يَقُولُوا أَجْمَعْنَا عَلَى هَذَا إِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْءُ مِنْ بَابِ الْقَوْلِ، أَوْ شُرُوعُهُمْ فِي الْفِعْلِ إِنْ كَانَ مِنْ بَابِهِ أَيْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْءُ مِنْ بَابِ الْفِعْلِ، كَمَا إِذَا شَرَعَ أَهْلُ الِاجْتِهَادِ جَمِيعًا فِي الْمُضَارَبَةِ أَوْ الْمُزَارَعَةِ أَوْ الشَّرِكَةِ كَانَ ذَلِكَ إِجْمَاعًا مِنْهُمْ عَلَى شَرْعِيَّتِهَا. وَرُخْصَةٌ وَهُوَ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمَ أَوْ يَفْعَلَ الْبَعْضُ دُونَ الْبَعْضِ، أَنَّ اتَّفَقَ بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى قَوْلٍ أَوْ فِعْلٍ وَسَكَتَ الْبَاقُونَ مِنْهُمْ وَلَا يَرُدُّونَ عَلَيْهِمْ بَعْدَ مَضَيِّ مُدَّةِ التَّأَمُّلِ وَهِيَ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ أَوْ مَجْلِسُ الْعِلْمِ. وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا إِجْمَاعًا سُكُوتِيًّا وَهُوَ مَقْبُولٌ عِنْدَنَا وَفِيهِ خِلَافُ الشَّافِعِيِّ، لِأَنَّ السُّكُوتَ كَمَا يَكُونُ لِلْمُوَافَقَةِ يَكُونُ لِلْمُخَالَفَةِ وَلَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى الرِّضَا، كَمَا رُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ خَالَفَ عُمَرَ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْعَوْلِ فَقِيلَ لَهُ هَلْ أَظْهَرْتَ حُجَّتَكَ عَلَى عُمَرَ؟ قَالَ: كَانَ رَجُلًا مَهِيبًا فَهَيْبَتُهُ مَنَعَتْنِي رُؤْيَتَهُ. وَالْجَوَابُ: أَنَّ هَذَا غَيْرُ صَحِيحٍ لِأَنَّ عُمَرَ كَانَ شَدِيدَ الِانْقِيَادِ لِاسْتِمَاعِ الْحَقِّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ حَتَّى كَانَ يَقُولُ: لَا خَيْرَ فِيكُمْ مَا لَمْ تَقُولُوا وَلَا خَيْرَ فِيَّ مَا لَمْ أَسْمَعْ. وَكَيْفَ يُظَنُّ فِي حَقِّ الصَّحَابَةِ التَّقْصِيرُ فِي أُمُورِ الدِّينِ وَالسُّكُوتُ عَنِ الْحَقِّ فِي مَوْضِعِ الْحَاجَةِ؟ وَقَدْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: السَّاكِتُ عَنِ الْحَقِّ شَيْطَانٌ أَخْرَسُ.
Chapter of Consensus. It is linguistically 'agreement' and in the Shariah: the agreement of righteous mujtahids from the ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in one era on a verbal or practical matter. The pillar of consensus is of two types: definite resolve ('azimat) – which is their speaking what necessitates agreement, that all agree on the ruling by saying 'we have agreed on this' if the matter is verbal, or their beginning the action if it is of that category, i.e. the matter belongs to the category of action, such as when all the people of ijtihad begin mudarabah, muzara'ah, or partnership – that constitutes consensus from them on its legality. And a concession (rukhsah) – which is that some speak or act but not others, that some of them agree on a statement or action and the rest remain silent and do not reject them after the passage of the period of reflection, which is three days or a knowledge session. This is called 'silent consensus' and it is accepted by us (Hanafis), and there is disagreement from al-Shafi'i because silence can be for opposition as well as agreement and does not indicate satisfaction, as narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he disagreed with 'Umar on the issue of 'awl (increase in shares). It was said to him, 'Why did you not present your proof to 'Umar?' He said, 'He was an awe-inspiring man, his awe prevented me from seeing him.' The response: This is not correct because 'Umar was extremely compliant in listening to the truth from others, such that he would say, 'There is no good in you unless you speak, and no good in me unless I hear.' And how can deficiency in religious matters and silence about the truth when needed be imagined of the Companions? And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'The one who remains silent about the truth is a mute devil.'
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of Ijma (consensus) in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh. It begins with the linguistic and technical definition of Ijma: in language it means agreement, and in Shariah it is the agreement of the mujtahids of the Ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in a single era on a matter of sayings or actions. The author then divides Ijma into two types based on its 'rukn' (pillar): (1) 'Azimat (definite resolve) – this is when all mujtahids explicitly agree either verbally (e.g., saying 'we have agreed on this') or by all performing an action collectively (e.g., all of them entering into mudarabah contracts, which indicates their consensus on its legality). (2) Rukhsah (concession) – this is silent consensus (Ijma Sukuti), where some mujtahids express an opinion or perform an action and the rest remain silent after a period of reflection (defined as three days or the duration of a knowledge session). The Hanafi school accepts silent consensus as a binding proof, but Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that silence could be due to opposition or fear rather than agreement. The author refutes this by citing the example of Ibn Abbas and 'Umar, explaining that 'Umar was open to hearing the truth, and that Companions would not remain silent when the truth needed to be spoken; in fact, a hadith states that remaining silent about the truth is like a mute devil. Thus the Hanafi position is upheld.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-Ijma'): Agreement of the mujtahids of the Ummah in one era on a shar'i ruling.
العزيمة (al-'Azimat): The type of consensus where all mujtahids explicitly agree verbally or by action.
الرخصة (al-Rukhsah): The type of consensus where some mujtahids express a view and others remain silent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One day
B) Three days or a knowledge session
C) Seven days
D) One month

Key Takeaway
Ijma' is a definitive proof in Hanafi usul, and silent consensus is accepted as binding when no objection is raised after a period of reflection.

The Conditions of Ahl al-Ijma': Ijtihad and Righteousness
Positive statement of qualifications for ijma' participants with exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two core conditions for ahl al-ijma' according to the Hanafis and apply the exception for non-ijtihadi matters.

Core Idea
Ijma' requires consensus of mujtahid and righteous scholars; only in transmitted matters do commoners participate.

In this passage, the author sets forth the qualifications for those whose agreement constitutes binding consensus. The Hanafi view prioritizes juristic competence (ijtihad) and moral probity (salah), and distinguishes between ijtihadi matters and transmitted matters where commoners have a role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the opening statement: 'وَأَهْلُ الْإِجْمَاعِ مَنْ كَانَ مُجْتَهِدًا صَالِحًا' – the people of ijma' are those who are mujtahid and righteous. Note that both conditions are required.
Ijtihad ensures independent reasoning; salah ensures trustworthiness.
2
Note the exception
The text says 'إِلا فِيْمَا يُسْتَغْنَى فِيْهِ عَنِ الإِجْتِهَادِ' – except in matters where ijtihad is not needed. These are transmitted matters (like number of rak'ats, zakat amounts). In such cases, even commoners are considered, but any single opposition breaks consensus.
Examples: Quranic transmission, rak'at counts, zakat amounts, bread exchange, bathing.
3
Understand exclusion of commoners in ijtihadi matters
The author explains that in ijtihadi matters, only mujtahids count because commoners cannot form independent opinions; they must follow (taqlid). Their disagreement is not recognized.
This refutes the view that commoners' words suffice for ijma'.

Ashraf al-Anwar Sharh Urdu A, Light of Lights Volume 3. And the people of ijma' are those who are mujtahid and righteous, except in matters where ijtihad is not needed. There is no desire or sin in it; it is a description of his saying 'mujtahid' as he said: The people of ijma' are those who are mujtahid and righteous, except in matters where opinion is not needed, for in that, the people of ijtihad are not a condition, rather it is necessary to have meticulousness from every one of the elite and the commoners such that if one of them opposes, there is no ijma', like the transmission of the Quran, the numbers of rak'ats, the amounts of zakat, the exchange of bread, and taking a bath. And Abu Bakr al-Baqillani said that ijtihad is not a condition even in ijtihadi matters, and the statement of the commoners suffices for the formation of ijma'. The response: They are like cattle, and they must follow the mujtahids, and their opposition is not considered in what is obligatory for them of taqlid. And being from the Companions or from the 'Itrah (progeny) is not a condition. That is, some said there is no ijma' except from the Companions because the Prophet (peace be upon him) praised them and commended good, so they are the foundations in the knowledge of Shari'ah and the establishment of rulings. And some said there is no ijma' except from his 'Itrah (peace be upon him) and his relatives, because he said: 'I have left among you that which if you hold fast to, you will never go astray: the Book of Allah and my 'Itrah.' And with us, none of that is a condition, rather the mujtahid and righteous are sufficient in it. What you mentioned only indicates their virtue, not that their ijma' is a proof to the exclusion of others. Similarly, [the condition of] the people of Madinah or the extinction of their era. Malik said he conditions that they be from the people of Madinah because he said: 'Madinah expels its impurity as the bellows expels the dross of iron.' And the error also enters? So it would be expelled from it. And the people of ijma' — for the importance of ijma', being mujtahid and righteous is a condition, such that they have no deviation and no sin. However, in non-ijtihadi matters, being a mujtahid is not a condition for the people of consensus. The author's statement 'not in it mujtahid' is an explanation. Summary: Those who are pious and mujtahid are considered the people of ijma'. But in matters that do not require opinion (qiyas), the importance of ijtihad is not needed, but unity and agreement are needed among commoners and elite. So if one of them opposes, ijma' will not exist, like the transmission of the Quran, the numbers of rak'ats in prayer, the amounts of zakat, taking bread in exchange for bread as a loan, and bathing in the bathhouse, etc. And Abu Bakr al-Baqillani said that in ijtihadi matters too, ijtihad is not a condition, and the statement of the commoners is sufficient for the formation of ijma'. The response: Our response is that the commoners are like cattle (animals), and taqlid of a mujtahid is obligatory upon them.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage discusses the qualifications required for those whose consensus constitutes ijma'. The author first states that the people of ijma' must be mujtahid and righteous (salih). However, an exception is made for matters that do not require ijtihad, such as the transmission of the Quran, the number of rak'ats in prayer, and the amounts of zakat. In such non-ijtihadi matters, even common people (al-khawass wa al-'awamm) are considered, but any single opposition breaks the potential consensus. The author then refutes several alternative positions. First, Abu Bakr al-Baqillani argued that ijtihad is not required even for ijtihadi matters, and that the statements of commoners suffice. The Hanafi response is that commoners are like cattle; they are obligated to follow mujtahids, and their disagreement is not considered. Second, some scholars claimed that only the Companions could form ijma' because of the Prophet's praise, or only the 'Itrah (the Prophet's family) due to the hadith of thaqalayn. The author rejects these, stating that such texts indicate their virtue, not that their ijma' is uniquely authoritative; any righteous mujtahid qualifies. Third, Imam Malik conditioned ijma' on the people of Madinah because of a hadith that Madinah purges its impurities. The author critiques this as well, implying the Hanafi position that the only conditions are ijtihad and righteousness, regardless of time, place, or lineage.

Key Terms
أهل الإجماع (ahl al-ijma'): Those whose consensus constitutes ijma', must be mujtahid and salih in ijtihadi matters; in non-ijtihadi matters, includes all Muslims.
مجتهد (mujtahid): One qualified to derive rulings directly from sources; condition for ijma' participant in ijtihadi matters.
عوام ('awamm): Commoners, lay Muslims not qualified for ijtihad; not counted in ijtihadi ijma'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is required for a person to be considered part of ahl al-ijma' in an ijtihadi matter?
A) Being a Muslim and adult
B) Being a Companion of the Prophet
C) Being mujtahid and righteous
D) Being from Madinah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions ijma' on the participants being mujtahid and righteous in ijtihadi matters, but requires unanimity of all Muslims in transmitted matters.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate

Refuting Alternative Views on Ahl al-Ijma'
Refutation of alternative conditions for ijma' participants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttals to the views of al-Baqillani, exclusivity of Sahaba/'Itrah, and the Maliki condition of Madinah regarding ijma' participants.

Core Idea
Only mujtahid and righteous scholars qualify for ijma'; alternative conditions (commoners, Sahaba, 'Itrah, Madinah) are rejected as insufficient or misguided.

After stating the positive conditions, the author addresses three alternative propositions that would restrict ijma' to certain groups. Each is refuted with a combination of textual evidence and logical reasoning, affirming the Hanafi position that ijtihad and righteousness are the only necessary qualifications.

Guided Path
1
Analyze Baqillani's view
Baqillani argued that ijtihad is not required even in ijtihadi matters; commoners' agreement suffices. The Hanafi response: commoners are like cattle, obligated to follow mujtahids, and their opposition is irrelevant.
This highlights the epistemological role of ijtihad: consensus must be based on knowledge, not mere opinion.
2
Examine conditions of Sahaba or 'Itrah
Some argued that only Companions or the Prophet's family ('Itrah) can form ijma'. The Hanafi response: texts praising them indicate virtue, not exclusive authority. Righteous mujtahids from any generation suffice.
The hadith of thaqalayn is interpreted as a call to honor the family, not as a restriction on ijma'.
3
Consider the Maliki condition
Imam Malik conditioned ijma' on the people of Madinah based on a hadith about Madinah purifying impurity. The author implies this is rejected, as no such condition is accepted in the Hanafi school.
This shows regional or temporal restrictions are not recognized.

Commentary
This passage discusses the qualifications required for those whose consensus constitutes ijma'. The author first states that the people of ijma' must be mujtahid and righteous (salih). However, an exception is made for matters that do not require ijtihad, such as the transmission of the Quran, the number of rak'ats in prayer, and the amounts of zakat. In such non-ijtihadi matters, even common people (al-khawass wa al-'awamm) are considered, but any single opposition breaks the potential consensus. The author then refutes several alternative positions. First, Abu Bakr al-Baqillani argued that ijtihad is not required even for ijtihadi matters, and that the statements of commoners suffice. The Hanafi response is that commoners are like cattle; they are obligated to follow mujtahids, and their disagreement is not considered. Second, some scholars claimed that only the Companions could form ijma' because of the Prophet's praise, or only the 'Itrah (the Prophet's family) due to the hadith of thaqalayn. The author rejects these, stating that such texts indicate their virtue, not that their ijma' is uniquely authoritative; any righteous mujtahid qualifies. Third, Imam Malik conditioned ijma' on the people of Madinah because of a hadith that Madinah purges its impurities. The author critiques this as well, implying the Hanafi position that the only conditions are ijtihad and righteousness, regardless of time, place, or lineage.

Key Terms
أهل الإجماع (ahl al-ijma'): Those whose consensus constitutes ijma'; must be mujtahid and salih in ijtihadi matters.
العوام (al-'awamm): Commoners, lay Muslims; cannot form ijma' in ijtihadi matters, must practice taqlid.
العترة (al-'itrah): The Prophet's family; some consider their ijma' exclusive, Hanafis say virtue not exclusivity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects any condition for ijma' beyond ijtihad and righteousness, refuting alternative views that would restrict it to commoners, Sahaba, 'Itrah, or Madinans.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate

Conditions for the People of Ijma: Ijtihad and Righteousness
Defining who qualifies as people of ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a person to be considered a member of Ahl al-Ijma and distinguish between ijtihadi and non-ijtihadi matters in the Hanafi view.

Core Idea
For matters requiring ijtihad, only mujtahid and righteous scholars count; for plain matters, all Muslims matter.

In this passage, the author defines who constitutes the people of consensus (Ahl al-Ijma). He states that consensus is a binding proof, but not every Muslim's opinion counts. There are conditions: the person must be a mujtahid and righteous, free from desire and transgression. However, for matters that do not require ijtihad – such as the transmission of the Qur'an, numbers of rak'ahs, etc. – even the common people's agreement is considered. The author then refutes a counter-argument from al-Baqillani who claimed that ijtihad is not even required for ijtihadi matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the definition
The passage defines 'Ahl al-Ijma'. Determine who they are according to the text.
The definition is: 'the people of consensus are those who are a mujtahid and righteous'.
2
Understand the conditions for ijtihadi matters
Note the conditions: must be mujtahid and righteous (salih), free from desire and transgression.
This applies to matters requiring ijtihad.
3
Recognize the exception for non-ijtihadi matters
In matters that are clear and do not require independent reasoning (like Qur'an transmission, rak'ah counts, zakat amounts), the condition of ijtihad is not required; rather, the consensus of all Muslims, both elite and common, is considered.
Even one opposing voice prevents ijma in these matters.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of al-Baqillani
Al-Baqillani argued that ijtihad is not a condition even in ijtihadi matters. The Hanafi response: commoners are like cattle; they must follow mujtahids, and their opposition is not counted.
The practical effect: only mujtahids matter for ijtihadi ijma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَهْلُ الْإِجْمَاعِ مَنْ كَانَ مُجْتَهِدًا صَالِحًا إِلَّا فِيمَا يُسْتَغْنَى فِيهِ عَنِ الْإِجْتِهَادِ لَيْسَ فِيهِ هُوًى وَلَا فِسْقًا صِفَةٌ لِقَوْلِهِ مُجْتَهِدًا كَأَنَّهُ قَالَ أَهْلُ الْإِجْمَاعِ مَنْ كَانَ مُجْتَهِدًا صَالِحًا إِلَّا فِيمَا يُسْتَغْنَى عَنِ الرَّأْيِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَشْتَرِطُ فِيهِ أَهْلُ الْإِجْتِهَادِ بَلْ لَا بُدَّ فِيهِ مِنْ إِتْقَانِ كُلٍّ مِنَ الْخَوَاصِّ وَالْعَوَامِّ حَتَّى لَوْ خَالَفَ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمْ لَمْ يَكُنْ إِجْمَاعًا كَنَقْلِ الْقُرْآنِ وَأَعْدَادِ الرَّكْعَاتِ وَمَقَادِيرِ الزَّكَاةِ وَاسْتِعْرَاضِ الْخُبْزِ وَالاِسْتِحْمَامِ. وَقَالَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ الْبَاقِلَّانِيُّ أَنَّ الْإِجْتِهَادَ لَيْسَ بِشَرْطٍ فِي الْمَسَائِلِ الْإِجْتِهَادِيَّةِ أَيْضًا وَيَكْفِي قَوْلُ الْعَوَامِّ فِي انْعِقَادِ الْإِجْمَاعِ. وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّهُمْ كَالْأَنْعَامِ وَعَلَيْهِمْ أَنْ يُقَلِّدُوا الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ خِلَافُهُمْ فِيمَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنَ التَّقْلِيدِ.
The people of consensus are those who are a mujtahid and righteous, except in what does not require ijtihad. There is no desire and no transgression. A description for his saying 'mujtahid': as if he said: the people of consensus are those who are a mujtahid and righteous, except in what does not require opinion, for ijtihad is not required in it; rather it is necessary in it to have proficiency of every one of the elite and the common, so that if one of them opposes, it is not consensus, like the transmission of the Qur'an, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of zakat, the exchange of bread, and bathing. Abu Bakr al-Baqillani said that ijtihad is not a condition in ijtihadi issues as well, and the statement of the common people suffices for the formation of consensus. The answer: that they are like cattle, and they must imitate the mujtahids, and their opposition is not considered in what is obligatory upon them of taqlid.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a definition of who constitutes the people of ijma. The author states that the people of consensus are those who are mujtahid and righteous, free from desire and transgression. This condition applies to matters that require ijtihad (opinion). However, in matters that do not require ijtihad, such as the transmission of the Qur'an, the numbers of rak'ahs in prayer, the amounts of zakat, and other such matters where the ruling is known from clear texts and does not require reasoning, ijtihad is not a condition. In such matters, the consensus of all Muslims, both elite and common, is considered, and even one opposing voice prevents consensus. The passage then mentions the view of Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, who argued that ijtihad is not even a condition in ijtihadi issues, and that the agreement of common people suffices for the formation of consensus. The Hanafi response is that common people are like cattle; they are not qualified to form independent opinions and must follow the mujtahids. Their opposition in matters where they are obligated to follow is not counted.

Key Terms
مُجْتَهِد (mujtahid): A scholar qualified to derive rulings from the primary sources through ijtihad.
صَالِح (salih): Righteous, free from transgression and desire.
أهل الإجماع (Ahl al-Ijma): The people whose unanimous agreement constitutes binding ijma; in ijtihadi matters, they must be mujtahid and righteous; in non-ijtihadi matters, they include all Muslims.
عوام (awamm): Common Muslims who are not qualified to perform ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, what is the condition for a person to be counted among the people of ijma in matters requiring ijtihad?
A) Being a mujtahid and righteous, free from desire and transgression
B) Being a Companion of the Prophet
C) Being from the Ahl al-Bayt
D) Being from the people of Madinah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view: In ijtihadi matters, only mujtahid and righteous scholars constitute Ahl al-Ijma; in non-ijtihadi matters, universal consensus of all Muslims is required.

Rejecting Conditions of Companionship, Ahl al-Bayt, and Madinah for Ijma
Refuting conditions of being from Sahaba, Ahl al-Bayt, or Madinah for ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the conditions for ijma and evaluate the proofs for restricting ijma to Companions, Ahl al-Bayt, or Madinah.

Core Idea
Ijma is not restricted to Companions, Ahl al-Bayt, or Madinah; any righteous mujtahid can form binding consensus.

Some scholars have argued that only the consensus of the Companions, the Ahl al-Bayt, or the people of Madinah is authoritative. This lesson examines these claims and the Hanafi response, which holds that such conditions are not required. Instead, the consensus of any group of righteous mujtahids is binding. Understanding this debate clarifies the scope of ijma as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed conditions
Locate the three groups that some scholars require for ijma: the Companions, the Ahl al-Bayt, and the people of Madinah. Note the proofs cited for each.
These conditions are mentioned in the first parts of the passage.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rejects all three conditions. The passage states 'according to us, none of that is a condition' and that 'righteous mujtahids suffice'.
The Hanafi principle is that ijtihad and righteousness, not group membership, are key.
3
Analyze the opposing proofs
For each condition, identify the dalil: for Companions, the Prophet's praise; for Ahl al-Bayt, the Hadith al-Thaqalayn; for Madinah, the hadith about Madinah expelling wickedness.
These are naqli proofs (dalil naqli).
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that these proofs only indicate the virtue of those groups, not that their consensus is exclusively binding. The response distinguishes between virtue and legal authority.
This is the core of the Hanafi rebuttal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a consensus of non-Companion, non-Madinan mujtahids is binding according to the Hanafi school, but not according to those who impose the conditions.
This shows how the difference affects actual fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَوْنُهُ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ أَوْ مِنَ الْعِتْرَةِ لَا يُشْتَرَطُ يَعْنِي قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ لَا إِجْمَاعَ إِلَّا لِلصَّحَابَةِ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مَدَحَهُمْ وَأَثْنَى عَلَيْهِمْ الْخَيْرَ فَهُمُ الْأُصُولُ فِي عِلْمِ الشَّرِيعَةِ وَانْعِقَادِ الْأَحْكَامِ فَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ لَا إِجْمَاعَ إِلَّا لِعِتْرَتِهِ وَأَهْلِ قَرَابَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ قَالَ إِنِّي تَرَكْتُ فِيكُمْ مَا إِنْ تَمَسَّكْتُمْ بِهِ لَنْ تَضِلُّوا: كِتَابَ اللَّهِ وَعِتْرَتِي وَعِنْدَنَا شَيْءٌ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لَيْسَ بِشَرْطٍ بَلْ يَكْفِي الْمُجْتَهِدُونَ الصَّالِحُونَ فِيهِ وَمَا ذَكَرْتُمْ إِنَّمَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى فَضْلِهِمْ لَا عَلَى أَنَّ إِجْمَاعَهُمْ حُجَّةٌ دُونَ غَيْرِهِمْ وَكَذَا أَهْلُ الْمَدِينَةِ أَوِ انْقِرَاضُ عَصْرِهِمْ قَالَ مَالِكٌ يَشْتَرِطُ فِيهِ كَوْنَهُمْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ لِأَنَّهُ قَالَ إِنَّ الْمَدِينَةَ تَنْفِي خُبْثَهَا كَمَا يَنْفِي الْكِيرُ الْحَدِيدَ وَالْخَطَأُ أَيْضًا خُبْثٌ فَيَكُونُ مَنْفِيًّا عَنْهَا وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ لِفَضْلِهِمْ وَلَا يَكُونُ دَلِيلًا عَلَى أَنَّ إِجْمَاعَهُمْ حُجَّةٌ لَا غَيْرَ
And being from the Companions or from the family (al-itrah) is not a condition. Meaning, some said: there is no consensus except for the Companions because the Prophet praised them and commended good upon them, so they are the foundations in the knowledge of the Sharia and the formation of rulings. And some said: there is no consensus except for his family and his relatives because he said: 'I have left among you that which if you hold fast to it, you will never go astray: the Book of Allah and my family.' And according to us, none of that is a condition, rather righteous mujtahids suffice. And what you mentioned only indicates their virtue, not that their consensus is a proof to the exclusion of others. Likewise, the people of Madinah or the passing of their era. Malik required that they be from the people of Madinah because he said: 'Verily Madinah expels its wickedness as the bellows expels the iron, and error is also wickedness, so it is expelled from it.' The answer: that is for their virtue, and it is not evidence that their consensus is a proof exclusively.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage addresses two conditions some scholars have imposed for the validity of ijma: being from the Companions, and being from the Ahl al-Bayt (the Prophet's family). Those who require Companionship argue that the Prophet praised them and they are the primary source of Shari'a knowledge. Those who require being from the Ahl al-Bayt cite the hadith of the 'Thaqalayn'. The Hanafi position rejects both as conditions, saying that righteous mujtahids from any generation suffice. These conditions only indicate the virtue of these groups, not that their consensus alone is a proof. The passage then mentions the view of Imam Malik that ijma requires the consensus of the people of Madinah, based on a hadith that Madinah purifies its people from error. The Hanafi response is the same: this indicates their virtue, not exclusivity.

Key Terms
الصَّحَابَة (al-sahabah): The Companions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
الْعِتْرَة (al-itrah): The family of the Prophet, specifically his descendants and relatives.
أَهْلُ الْمَدِينَة (ahl al-madinah): The people of Madinah, particularly the scholars among them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the necessary condition for the validity of ijma?
A) All participants must be from the Companions.
B) All participants must be from the Ahl al-Bayt.
C) All participants must be righteous mujtahids.
D) All participants must be from the people of Madinah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects any restriction of ijma to Companions, Ahl al-Bayt, or Madinans; virtue does not equal exclusive authority.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate

Hanafi View on Inqirad al-Asr and Later Ijma
Stating Shafi'i condition and Hanafi rule on later ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on inqirad al-asr and explain how later ijma can override prior ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Ijma is binding upon agreement, not upon death; later consensus can resolve earlier disagreements.

This passage presents two key usul disputes involving ijma. First, the Shafi'i requirement of inqirad al-asr (passing of the age) for consensus to be binding, which the Hanafis reject. Second, the question whether a later consensus can override a prior disagreement among mujtahids. The correct Hanafi view affirms that later ijma is valid and removes the earlier ikhtilaf, as illustrated by the historical example of selling an umm walad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Read the passage and note that it first discusses the Shafi'i condition of inqirad al-asr, then addresses the validity of later ijma when there was prior disagreement.
These are two separate but related conditions.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i argument on inqirad al-asr
Al-Shafi'i requires that all mujtahids of that generation die before their consensus is considered final. Understand his reasoning: a living mujtahid might change his view.
Hanafis do not accept this condition.
3
Examine the reported restriction on later ijma
Some claim that Abu Hanifa requires absence of prior disagreement for later ijma. The text clarifies this is incorrect (laysa kathalika).
The correct view is that later ijma is valid.
4
Study the example of umm walad
Abu Hanifa ruled selling an umm walad impermissible; Ali (RA) permitted it. Later consensus formed on impermissibility. According to Imam Muhammad, a judge's verdict permitting the sale would not be enforceable.
This shows the effect of later ijma: it nullifies earlier contrary positions.
5
Apply the rule
The later consensus becomes binding; any earlier disagreement is effectively overturned. A judge ruling against this consensus would have his verdict invalidated.
This is the practical thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَشْتَرِطُ فِيهِ انْقِرَاضَ الْعَصْرِ وَمَوْتَ جَمِيعِ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ فَلَا يَكُونُ إِجْمَاعُهُمْ حُجَّةً مَا لَمْ يَمُوتُوا. وَقِيلَ يَشْتَرِطُ لِلْإِجْمَاعِ اللَّاحِقِ عَدَمُ الِاخْتِلَافِ السَّابِقِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، يَعْنِي إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ أَهْلُ عَصْرٍ فِي مَسْأَلَةٍ وَمَاتُوا عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ يُرِيدُ مَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ أَنْ يَجْمَعُوا عَلَى قَوْلٍ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهَا، قِيلَ لَا يَجُوزُ ذَلِكَ الْإِجْمَاعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَلَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ بَلِ الصَّحِيحُ أَنَّهُ يَنْعَقِدُ عِنْدَهُ إِجْمَاعُ مُتَأَخِّرٍ وَيَرْتَفِعُ الْخِلَافُ السَّابِقُ مِنَ الْبَيْنِ وَنَظِيرُهُ مَسْأَلَةُ بَيْعِ أُمِّ الْوَلَدِ فَإِنَّهُ عِنْدَهُ لَا يَجُوزُ وَعِنْدَ عَلِيٍّ يَجُوزُ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ أَجْمَعُوا عَلَى عَدَمِ جَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا فَإِنْ قَضَى الْقَاضِي بِجَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا لَا يَنْفُذُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّهَا مُخَالِفَةٌ لِلْإِجْمَاعِ اللَّاحِقِ.
Al-Shafi'i requires in it the passing of the age and the death of all mujtahids, so their consensus is not a proof as long as they have not died. And it was said that for later consensus, the absence of prior disagreement is required according to Abu Hanifa, meaning if the people of an age disagreed on a matter and died upon it, then those after them want to agree on one of the opinions, it is said that this consensus is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. But that is not correct; rather the correct view is that according to him, later consensus is formed and the prior disagreement is removed. An example is the issue of selling an umm walad: according to him [Abu Hanifa] it is not permissible, but according to Ali it is permissible. Then after that, they agreed on the impermissibility of selling her. So if a judge judges its permissibility, it is not executed according to Muhammad because it contradicts the later consensus.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage discusses two conditions. First, the Shafi'i view that ijma is only binding after the death of all mujtahids of that generation; while they are alive, their consensus is not final because they might change their views. The Hanafi school does not require the passing of the age. Second, a reported view about Abu Hanifa's position on later consensus when there was prior disagreement. The correct Hanafi view is that later consensus is valid and removes the previous disagreement. The example given is the sale of an umm walad: Abu Hanifa held it impermissible, Ali (RA) allowed it, then later scholars agreed on its impermissibility. According to Imam Muhammad, a judge's verdict permitting such sale would not be enforceable because it contradicts the later consensus.

Key Terms
انْقِرَاضُ الْعَصْرِ (inqirad al-asr): The passing of the entire generation of mujtahids (by death).
إِجْمَاعٌ لَاحِق (ijma' lahiq): A consensus formed by later mujtahids after a period of disagreement.
خِلَافٌ سَابِق (khilaf sabiq): Disagreement among earlier mujtahids on a specific issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Regarding the requirement of 'passing of the age' (inqirad al-asr) for ijma, what is the Hanafi position?
A) Ijma is only binding after all mujtahids of that generation have died
B) Ijma is binding as soon as the mujtahids agree, regardless of death
C) Ijma is not binding at all
D) Ijma requires the agreement of the Ahl al-Bayt

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ijma is binding immediately upon agreement; later consensus can resolve earlier disagreements, as shown by the umm walad example.
