Refuting Personal and Geographical Conditions for Ijma
Refuting conditions that restrict Ijma to specific groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions that require mujtahids to be from the Sahaba, Ahl al-Bayt, or Madinans, and refute them using the Hanafi principle that virtue does not entail exclusivity.

Core Idea
Ijma requires righteous mujtahids, not membership in special groups.

Some scholars argued that Ijma is only valid if the mujtahids are Companions, the Prophet's household, or residents of Madinah. This lesson examines their claims and shows why the Hanafi school rejects them, establishing that the consensus of any qualified mujtahids is sufficient for a binding ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed conditions
List the three conditions: being from the Sahaba, from the Ahl al-Bayt, or from the people of Madinah.
These are external restrictions on who can participate in Ijma.
2
Examine the arguments for each condition
For Sahaba/Ahl al-Bayt: the Hadith of Thaqalayn and the Prophet's praise. For Madinans: the hadith that Madinah purifies its people.
Understand the proof offered by proponents.
3
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
The Hanafi response distinguishes between virtue (fadl) and exclusive authority. The texts show the virtue of these groups but do not prove that their consensus alone is hujjah.
Key principle: virtue does not make their consensus exclusive.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
Conclude that Ijma is valid from any righteous mujtahids, regardless of lineage or location.
This maintains the continuity and universality of Ijma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نور الانوار جلد سوم

اشرف الانوار شرح اردو ہوتی ہے اور جن امور میں ان پر تقلید واجب ہوتی ہے ان میں ان کے اختلاف کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ وكونه من الصحابة أو من العترة ولا يشترط اور اجماع کی اہمیت کے لئے صحابہ یا اہل بیت ہونا شرط نہیں یعنی بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اجتماع کے لئے صحابہ کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ بغیر صحابہ کے اجماع نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اسکی تعریف فرمائی ہے اور ان کے حق میں نیک خبر دی ہے۔ لہذا شرعی علوم اور نقد و احکام کے لئے وہی اصل ہیں اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اجتماع درست نہیں۔ مگر صرف اہل بیت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا اجماع یعنی ان کے اہل بیت اور قرابت داروں کا اجماع ہی معتبر ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ میں نے تمھارے اندر ایسی چیز چھوڑی ہے کہ جب تک تم ان کو مضبوطی سے پکڑے رہو گے۔ ہر گز گمراہ نہ ہو گے ۔ اول کتاب اللہ دوسرے اہل بیت ہیں اور ہمارے نزدیک ان میں سے کوئی بھی شرط نہیں ہے۔ (یعنی نہ صحابی ہونا اور نہ اہل بیت رسول ہونا، نہ اہل قرابت رسول ہونا ) بلکہ اجماع کے لئے نیک صالح مجتہدین کا اجماع کافی ہے اور جو امور ان بعض لوگوں نے بیان کئے ہیں وہ ان کی ذاتی اور خاندانی فضیلت ہے۔ اس لئے نہیں کہ ان کا اجماع حجت ہے دوسروں کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے وكذا اهل المدينة او انقراض العصر الى طرح اہل مدینہ ہو یا زمانے کا ختم ہونا بھی شرط نہیں ہے یعنی اجماع کی اہمیت کے لئے مدینہ کا باشندہ ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ حضرت امام مالک رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اجتماع میں شرط ہے ان علماء کا اہل مدینہ ہونا شرط ہے اور دلیل یہ دیتے ہیں ان المدينة تنفى خبثها الخ۔ مدینہ گندگی اور میل کو اس ح پھینک دیتا ہے جس طرح بھٹی لوہے کے میل کو دور کر دیتی ہے اور اجتہاد میں خطاء کرنا بھی ایک میل ہے لہذا اہل مدینہ کا اجماع بے خطا ہو گا اور اس کا اختیار بھی کیا جائے گا۔ وَالْجَوَابُ أَنْ ذِأَلِكَ لَفَضلِهِمْ وَلَا يَكُونَ دَلِيْلاً عَلَىٰ أَنْ إِجْمَاعَهُمْ حُجَّةٌ لَا غَيْرَ وَقَالَ الشافَعِي يَسْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ اِنْقِراضَ الْعَصْرِ وَمَوْتُ جَمِيعِ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ فَلَا يَكُونُ إجْمَاعُهُمْ حَجَّةً مَالَمْ يَمُوتُوا وَقِيْلَ يَسْتَرِطُ لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق عَدَمُ الاِخْتِلَافِ السابق عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنَّيْفَةَ يَعْنِي إِذا اخْتَلَفَ اهل عَصْرٍ فِي مَسْئَلَةٍ وَمَا تُوا عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ يُريدُ مَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ أَنْ يَجْمَعُوا عَلى قَوْلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهَا قِيلَ لَا يَجُوزُ ذالك الإجْمَاعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةٌ وَلَيْسَ كَذلِكَ فِى الصحيح بَلِ الصَّحِيحَ أَنَّهُ يَنْعَقِدُ عِنْدَهُ إِجْمَاعُ مُتَأَخِرُ وَيَرْتَفِعُ الخلاف السَّابِقُ مِنْ الْبَيْنِ وَنَظِيْرُهُ مَسألة بَيْع أم الوَلَدِ فَإِنَّهُ عِنْدَ لا يَجُوزُ وَعِنْدَ عَلِي يَجُوزُ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ أَجْمَعُوا عَلَىٰ عَدَمٍ جَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا فَإِنْ قضى الْقَاضِي بِجَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا لَا يَنْقَدْ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّهُ مُخَالِف لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق

اشرف الانوار شرح برود
نور الانوار جلد سوم

وَيَجُوزُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنَيْفَةَ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْكَرْخِي عَنْهُ لِأَهْلِ الْاِخْتِلَافِ السَّابِقِ وَأَبُويُوسُف فِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَهُ وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالشَّرْطُ إِجْمَاعُ الكُلِّ وَخِلافُ الْوَاحِدِ مَانِعَ خِلافِ الأكثر يَعْنِي فَى حِينِ انْعِقَادِ الإِجْمَاعِ لَوْ خَالَفَ وَاحِدٌ كَانَ خِلافُهُ معتبرًا وَلَا يَنْعَقِدُ الإجماع لأن لفظ الأُمَّةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لَا تَجْتَمِعُ أُمْتِي عَلى الصَّلَالَةِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الكُلِّ فَيَحْتَمِلُ أنْ يَكُونَ الصَّوابُ مَعَ مُخَالِف وَقَالَ بَعْضُ المُعْتَزِلَةِ يَنْعَقِدُ الإِجْمَاعُ بِاتِّفَاقِ الأكثرِ لأَنْ الْحَقِّ مَعَ الْجَمَاعَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السلام يَدُ اللهِ عَلَى الْجَمَاعَةِ فَمَنْ شَذَّ شَذَ فِي النَّارِ وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّ مَعْنَاهُ بَعْدَ تَحَقَّقِ الإِجْمَاعِ مَنْ شَذَّ وَخَرَجَ مَنْهُ دَخَلَ فِي النَّارِ. ترجمه تشریح والجواب : جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ اس سے اہل مدینہ کی فضیلت تو ثابت ہوتی ہے مگر اس سے لازم نہیں آتا کہ انہیں کا اجماع حجت غیر اہل مدینہ کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے ۔ فقال الشافعی رحمہ اللہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں۔ اجماع کے منعقد ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مجتہدین کا دور ختم ہو جائے اور مجتہدین باقی نہ ر ہیں وفات پا جائیں۔ لہذا جب تک وہ وفات نہ پائیں ان کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے کیونکہ موت سے پہلے رجوع کا احتمال باقی رہتا ہے اور احتمال رجوع کے ہوتے ہوئے کسی رائے پر پر ترانہ رہنا ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ جواب ہم جواب دیں گے اجماع کے حجت ہونے پر جو نصوص دلالت کرتی ہیں۔ ان میں اہل اجماع کی موت اور تا عدم موت میں کوئی فرق وارد نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اجتماع کے حجت ہونے میں اس کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے ۔ وقِيلَ يُسْتَرَطُ لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک زمانہ سابق میں اختلاف نہ ہونا شرط ہے بعد والوں کے اجماع کے ممبر ہونے کے لئے یعنی جب اهل ایک زمانے کے علاوہ مجتہدین کسی مسئلے میں اختلاف کریں اور پھر اس پر وفات پا جائیں پھر ان کے بعد علماء مجتہدین ارادہ کریں کہ ان کے کسی قول پر اجماع کر لیں تو کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ اجتماع امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ وليس كذالك في الصحیح۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی طرف اس قول کی نسبت ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ صحیح رائے حضرت امام صاحب کی یہ ہے کہ بعد والوں کا اجتماع درست ہے۔ تاکہ سابق اختلاف در میان سے دور ہو جائے اور اس کی نظیر ام ولد کی بیع کا مسئلہ ہے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کی بیع حضرت عمر کے نزدیک نا جائز اور حضرت علی کے نزدیک جائز ہے، پھر اس کے بعد والوں نے اس مسئلہ پر اجماع کیا کہ بیچ ام ولد کی جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اگر قاضی اس کے بیچ کا فیصلہ کر دے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ اجماع لاحق کے خلاف ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ام ولد کی بیع جائز ہے امام کرخی کی ایک روایت میں سابق اختلاف کی وجہ سے جائز ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں امام ابو یوسف بھی ان کے ساتھ ہیں اور ایک روایت میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں۔
Nur al-Anwar Volume 3. Ashraf al-Anwar is an Urdu commentary. In matters where taqlid upon them is obligatory, their disagreement is not considered. 'And that he be from the Companions or from the Ahl al-Bayt is not a condition.' For the importance of Ijma, being a Companion or Ahl al-Bayt is not a condition. Some said that for consensus, being a Companion is a condition; without Companions, no consensus. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) praised them and gave good news regarding them. Therefore they are the foundation for religious sciences and criticism and rulings. And some said consensus is not valid except only the consensus of the Ahl al-Bayt, i.e., his household and relatives, because the Prophet said: 'I have left among you something; as long as you hold fast to it, you will never go astray: first the Book of Allah, second my Ahl al-Bayt.' And according to us, none of these is a condition (i.e., neither being a Companion nor being of the Ahl al-Bayt nor being a relative). Rather, for Ijma, the consensus of righteous mujtahids is sufficient. And the matters that some people have mentioned are their personal and family virtue, not that their consensus is hujjah and others' consensus is not. Likewise, being from Madinah or the extinction of the age is also not a condition. That is, for the validity of Ijma, being a resident of Madinah is not a condition, as Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said that a condition for consensus is that the scholars be from Madinah. They give as proof: 'Madinah expels its impurities like the furnace removes the dross of iron.' Error in ijtihad is also an impurity, so the consensus of the people of Madinah will be infallible and must be followed. The answer: That is for their virtue, and it does not prove that their consensus is hujjah exclusively. And al-Shafi'i condition is the extinction of the age and the death of all mujtahids; their consensus is not hujjah until they die. And it is said that for later consensus, the absence of prior disagreement is a condition according to Abu Hanifa. That is, if the people of an era differed on a matter and then died, and then those after them intend to make consensus on one of those sayings, it is said this consensus is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. But this is not correct; rather the correct view is that later consensus is valid according to him and removes the previous disagreement. Its parallel is the issue of selling Umm al-Walad: it was not permissible according to Umar and permissible according to Ali. Then after that they made consensus that selling her is not permissible. So if a judge passes a judgment allowing her sale, according to Muhammad it is not executed because it contradicts the later consensus. And according to Abu Hanifa, in the narration of al-Karkhi from him, it is permissible due to the previous disagreement. And Abu Yusuf is with him in one narration, and with Muhammad in another. And the condition is the consensus of all, and the opposition of one prevents the opposition of the majority. That is, at the time of formation of Ijma, if one opposes, his opposition is considered, and Ijma is not formed because the word 'my community' in his saying (peace be upon him) 'My community will not agree upon error' encompasses all. So it is possible that the truth is with the opponent. And some Mu'tazila said that Ijma is formed by agreement of the majority because the truth is with the group, due to his saying: 'The Hand of Allah is with the group; whoever deviates, deviates into the Fire.' The answer: Its meaning is after Ijma is established, whoever deviates and leaves it enters the Fire. Translation/explanation: The answer to that is that it establishes the virtue of the people of Madinah, but it does not necessitate that their consensus alone is hujjah and others' is not. So al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The condition for the formation of Ijma is that the era of mujtahids ends and they die. Therefore, as long as they are alive, their consensus is not hujjah because before death there remains the possibility of retraction, and with the possibility of retraction, staying firm on an opinion is not established. We will answer: The texts that indicate Ijma is hujjah do not differentiate between the death of the people of Ijma and their non-death. From this it is known that this has no bearing on Ijma being hujjah. And it is said that for later consensus, the absence of prior disagreement is a condition according to Abu Hanifa, i.e., when the mujtahids of a past era differed on a matter and then died, and then later scholars intend to make consensus on one of those sayings, it is said this Ijma is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. But this is not correct; rather it is correct that his opinion is that later consensus is valid, so that the previous disagreement is removed. Its parallel is the issue of selling Umm al-Walad. Because selling Umm al-Walad was not permissible according to Umar and permissible according to Ali. Then those after them made consensus that selling Umm al-Walad is not permissible. Therefore, if a judge gives a judgment allowing her sale, according to Imam Muhammad the judgment will not be enforced because it contradicts the later consensus. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling Umm al-Walad is permissible, according to one narration from al-Karkhi due to the previous disagreement. And in one narration, Imam Abu Yusuf is with him, and in another narration he is with Imam Muhammad.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, addresses the conditions required for the validity of Ijma (consensus) in Hanafi usul. The author systematically refutes several conditions proposed by other schools or individuals. First, the condition that the mujtahids must be from the Sahaba (Companions) or Ahl al-Bayt (household of the Prophet) is rejected. While these groups have virtue, their consensus is not exclusively hujjah; the consensus of any righteous mujtahids suffices. Second, the condition that they must be from Madinah (Imam Malik's view) is similarly refuted: the virtue of Madinans does not prove exclusivity. Third, Imam Shafi'i's condition of inqirad al-asr (extinction of the age) is dismissed because the proofs for Ijma do not differentiate between the mujtahids being alive or dead. Finally, the passage discusses a controversial point attributed to Abu Hanifa: that later consensus cannot override a previous disagreement. The author clarifies that the correct Hanafi position is that later consensus is valid and removes the earlier ikhtilaf. The example of selling Umm al-Walad illustrates this: Umar and Ali differed, then later scholars agreed that it is impermissible. Imam Muhammad holds that a judge's ruling allowing sale would be invalid due to the later consensus, while Abu Hanifa (in one riwaya) allows it due to the previous disagreement. The passage also addresses the condition of unanimity: the word 'ummah' in the hadith encompasses all, so even one dissenter prevents Ijma, contra the Mu'tazila who accept majority consensus.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of all mujtahids of an era on a Shariah ruling
الصحابة (al-sahaba): The Companions of the Prophet Muhammad
أهل البيت (ahl al-bayt): The household of the Prophet, especially his family
أهل المدينة (ahl al-madinah): The residents of Madinah, especially scholars

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid condition for Ijma?
A) Mujtahids must be from the Sahaba.
B) Mujtahids must be from Madinah.
C) Mujtahids must be righteous and qualified, regardless of lineage or location.
D) Mujtahids must be from the Ahl al-Bayt.

Key Takeaway
Ijma is not restricted to special groups; the consensus of all righteous mujtahids is binding regardless of their lineage or location.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
6 min
Inqirad al-Asr: The Shafi'i Condition and Hanafi Response
Debating the necessity of extinction of the age for Ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i condition of inqirad al-asr (extinction of the era) for Ijma and state the Hanafi argument that it is not required.

Core Idea
Ijma is binding as soon as it is formed; the death of participants is irrelevant.

Imam al-Shafi'i famously conditioned the validity of Ijma on the death of all mujtahids in that era, arguing that until death, retraction is possible. This lesson examines that condition and the Hanafi counter-argument that the texts on Ijma do not distinguish between living and dead mujtahids.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i condition
Shafi'i required inqirad al-asr: all mujtahids of the era must have died for their consensus to be binding.
Rationale: possibility of retraction before death.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof
The possibility of retraction prevents certainty in the ruling while any participant is alive.
This is a methodological concern for the finality of Ijma.
3
Present the Hanafi refutation
The texts establishing Ijma as hujjah do not differentiate between life and death. The generality of the proofs includes Ijma formed by living mujtahids.
Key principle: lift of condition is not found in the sources.
4
Determine the practical consequence
In Hanafi, a consensus formed by living mujtahids is immediately binding. In Shafi'i, it is not binding until all die.
This affects whether a ruling can be acted upon immediately.

Source Text

نور الانوار جلد سوم

اشرف الانوار شرح اردو ہوتی ہے اور جن امور میں ان پر تقلید واجب ہوتی ہے ان میں ان کے اختلاف کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ وكونه من الصحابة أو من العترة ولا يشترط اور اجماع کی اہمیت کے لئے صحابہ یا اہل بیت ہونا شرط نہیں یعنی بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اجتماع کے لئے صحابہ کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ بغیر صحابہ کے اجماع نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اسکی تعریف فرمائی ہے اور ان کے حق میں نیک خبر دی ہے۔ لہذا شرعی علوم اور نقد و احکام کے لئے وہی اصل ہیں اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اجتماع درست نہیں۔ مگر صرف اہل بیت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا اجماع یعنی ان کے اہل بیت اور قرابت داروں کا اجماع ہی معتبر ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ میں نے تمھارے اندر ایسی چیز چھوڑی ہے کہ جب تک تم ان کو مضبوطی سے پکڑے رہو گے۔ ہر گز گمراہ نہ ہو گے ۔ اول کتاب اللہ دوسرے اہل بیت ہیں اور ہمارے نزدیک ان میں سے کوئی بھی شرط نہیں ہے۔ (یعنی نہ صحابی ہونا اور نہ اہل بیت رسول ہونا، نہ اہل قرابت رسول ہونا ) بلکہ اجماع کے لئے نیک صالح مجتہدین کا اجماع کافی ہے اور جو امور ان بعض لوگوں نے بیان کئے ہیں وہ ان کی ذاتی اور خاندانی فضیلت ہے۔ اس لئے نہیں کہ ان کا اجماع حجت ہے دوسروں کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے وكذا اهل المدينة او انقراض العصر الى طرح اہل مدینہ ہو یا زمانے کا ختم ہونا بھی شرط نہیں ہے یعنی اجماع کی اہمیت کے لئے مدینہ کا باشندہ ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ حضرت امام مالک رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اجتماع میں شرط ہے ان علماء کا اہل مدینہ ہونا شرط ہے اور دلیل یہ دیتے ہیں ان المدينة تنفى خبثها الخ۔ مدینہ گندگی اور میل کو اس ح پھینک دیتا ہے جس طرح بھٹی لوہے کے میل کو دور کر دیتی ہے اور اجتہاد میں خطاء کرنا بھی ایک میل ہے لہذا اہل مدینہ کا اجماع بے خطا ہو گا اور اس کا اختیار بھی کیا جائے گا۔ وَالْجَوَابُ أَنْ ذِأَلِكَ لَفَضلِهِمْ وَلَا يَكُونَ دَلِيْلاً عَلَىٰ أَنْ إِجْمَاعَهُمْ حُجَّةٌ لَا غَيْرَ وَقَالَ الشافَعِي يَسْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ اِنْقِراضَ الْعَصْرِ وَمَوْتُ جَمِيعِ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ فَلَا يَكُونُ إجْمَاعُهُمْ حَجَّةً مَالَمْ يَمُوتُوا وَقِيْلَ يَسْتَرِطُ لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق عَدَمُ الاِخْتِلَافِ السابق عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنَّيْفَةَ يَعْنِي إِذا اخْتَلَفَ اهل عَصْرٍ فِي مَسْئَلَةٍ وَمَا تُوا عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ يُريدُ مَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ أَنْ يَجْمَعُوا عَلى قَوْلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهَا قِيلَ لَا يَجُوزُ ذالك الإجْمَاعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةٌ وَلَيْسَ كَذلِكَ فِى الصحيح بَلِ الصَّحِيحَ أَنَّهُ يَنْعَقِدُ عِنْدَهُ إِجْمَاعُ مُتَأَخِرُ وَيَرْتَفِعُ الخلاف السَّابِقُ مِنْ الْبَيْنِ وَنَظِيْرُهُ مَسألة بَيْع أم الوَلَدِ فَإِنَّهُ عِنْدَ لا يَجُوزُ وَعِنْدَ عَلِي يَجُوزُ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ أَجْمَعُوا عَلَىٰ عَدَمٍ جَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا فَإِنْ قضى الْقَاضِي بِجَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا لَا يَنْقَدْ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّهُ مُخَالِف لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق

نور الانوار جلد سوم

وَيَجُوزُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنَيْفَةَ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْكَرْخِي عَنْهُ لِأَهْلِ الْاِخْتِلَافِ السَّابِقِ وَأَبُويُوسُف فِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَهُ وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالشَّرْطُ إِجْمَاعُ الكُلِّ وَخِلافُ الْوَاحِدِ مَانِعَ خِلافِ الأكثر يَعْنِي فَى حِينِ انْعِقَادِ الإِجْمَاعِ لَوْ خَالَفَ وَاحِدٌ كَانَ خِلافُهُ معتبرًا وَلَا يَنْعَقِدُ الإجماع لأن لفظ الأُمَّةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لَا تَجْتَمِعُ أُمْتِي عَلى الصَّلَالَةِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الكُلِّ فَيَحْتَمِلُ أنْ يَكُونَ الصَّوابُ مَعَ مُخَالِف وَقَالَ بَعْضُ المُعْتَزِلَةِ يَنْعَقِدُ الإِجْمَاعُ بِاتِّفَاقِ الأكثرِ لأَنْ الْحَقِّ مَعَ الْجَمَاعَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السلام يَدُ اللهِ عَلَى الْجَمَاعَةِ فَمَنْ شَذَّ شَذَ فِي النَّارِ وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّ مَعْنَاهُ بَعْدَ تَحَقَّقِ الإِجْمَاعِ مَنْ شَذَّ وَخَرَجَ مَنْهُ دَخَلَ فِي النَّارِ. ترجمه تشریح والجواب : جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ اس سے اہل مدینہ کی فضیلت تو ثابت ہوتی ہے مگر اس سے لازم نہیں آتا کہ انہیں کا اجماع حجت غیر اہل مدینہ کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے ۔ فقال الشافعی رحمہ اللہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں۔ اجماع کے منعقد ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مجتہدین کا دور ختم ہو جائے اور مجتہدین باقی نہ ر ہیں وفات پا جائیں۔ لہذا جب تک وہ وفات نہ پائیں ان کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے کیونکہ موت سے پہلے رجوع کا احتمال باقی رہتا ہے اور احتمال رجوع کے ہوتے ہوئے کسی رائے پر پر ترانہ رہنا ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ جواب ہم جواب دیں گے اجماع کے حجت ہونے پر جو نصوص دلالت کرتی ہیں۔ ان میں اہل اجماع کی موت اور تا عدم موت میں کوئی فرق وارد نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اجتماع کے حجت ہونے میں اس کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے ۔ وقِيلَ يُسْتَرَطُ لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک زمانہ سابق میں اختلاف نہ ہونا شرط ہے بعد والوں کے اجماع کے ممبر ہونے کے لئے یعنی جب اهل ایک زمانے کے علاوہ مجتہدین کسی مسئلے میں اختلاف کریں اور پھر اس پر وفات پا جائیں پھر ان کے بعد علماء مجتہدین ارادہ کریں کہ ان کے کسی قول پر اجماع کر لیں تو کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ اجتماع امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ وليس كذالك في الصحیح۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی طرف اس قول کی نسبت ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ صحیح رائے حضرت امام صاحب کی یہ ہے کہ بعد والوں کا اجتماع درست ہے۔ تاکہ سابق اختلاف در میان سے دور ہو جائے اور اس کی نظیر ام ولد کی بیع کا مسئلہ ہے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کی بیع حضرت عمر کے نزدیک نا جائز اور حضرت علی کے نزدیک جائز ہے، پھر اس کے بعد والوں نے اس مسئلہ پر اجماع کیا کہ بیچ ام ولد کی جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اگر قاضی اس کے بیچ کا فیصلہ کر دے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ اجماع لاحق کے خلاف ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ام ولد کی بیع جائز ہے امام کرخی کی ایک روایت میں سابق اختلاف کی وجہ سے جائز ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں امام ابو یوسف بھی ان کے ساتھ ہیں اور ایک روایت میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں۔
Nur al-Anwar Volume 3. Ashraf al-Anwar is an Urdu commentary. In matters where taqlid upon them is obligatory, their disagreement is not considered. 'And that he be from the Companions or from the Ahl al-Bayt is not a condition.' For the importance of Ijma, being a Companion or Ahl al-Bayt is not a condition. Some said that for consensus, being a Companion is a condition; without Companions, no consensus. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) praised them and gave good news regarding them. Therefore they are the foundation for religious sciences and criticism and rulings. And some said consensus is not valid except only the consensus of the Ahl al-Bayt, i.e., his household and relatives, because the Prophet said: 'I have left among you something; as long as you hold fast to it, you will never go astray: first the Book of Allah, second my Ahl al-Bayt.' And according to us, none of these is a condition (i.e., neither being a Companion nor being of the Ahl al-Bayt nor being a relative). Rather, for Ijma, the consensus of righteous mujtahids is sufficient. And the matters that some people have mentioned are their personal and family virtue, not that their consensus is hujjah and others' consensus is not. Likewise, being from Madinah or the extinction of the age is also not a condition. That is, for the validity of Ijma, being a resident of Madinah is not a condition, as Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said that a condition for consensus is that the scholars be from Madinah. They give as proof: 'Madinah expels its impurities like the furnace removes the dross of iron.' Error in ijtihad is also an impurity, so the consensus of the people of Madinah will be infallible and must be followed. The answer: That is for their virtue, and it does not prove that their consensus is hujjah exclusively. And al-Shafi'i condition is the extinction of the age and the death of all mujtahids; their consensus is not hujjah until they die. And it is said that for later consensus, the absence of prior disagreement is a condition according to Abu Hanifa. That is, if the people of an era differed on a matter and then died, and then those after them intend to make consensus on one of those sayings, it is said this consensus is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. But this is not correct; rather the correct view is that later consensus is valid according to him and removes the previous disagreement. Its parallel is the issue of selling Umm al-Walad: it was not permissible according to Umar and permissible according to Ali. Then after that they made consensus that selling her is not permissible. So if a judge passes a judgment allowing her sale, according to Muhammad it is not executed because it contradicts the later consensus. And according to Abu Hanifa, in the narration of al-Karkhi from him, it is permissible due to the previous disagreement. And Abu Yusuf is with him in one narration, and with Muhammad in another. And the condition is the consensus of all, and the opposition of one prevents the opposition of the majority. That is, at the time of formation of Ijma, if one opposes, his opposition is considered, and Ijma is not formed because the word 'my community' in his saying (peace be upon him) 'My community will not agree upon error' encompasses all. So it is possible that the truth is with the opponent. And some Mu'tazila said that Ijma is formed by agreement of the majority because the truth is with the group, due to his saying: 'The Hand of Allah is with the group; whoever deviates, deviates into the Fire.' The answer: Its meaning is after Ijma is established, whoever deviates and leaves it enters the Fire. Translation/explanation: The answer to that is that it establishes the virtue of the people of Madinah, but it does not necessitate that their consensus alone is hujjah and others' is not. So al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The condition for the formation of Ijma is that the era of mujtahids ends and they die. Therefore, as long as they are alive, their consensus is not hujjah because before death there remains the possibility of retraction, and with the possibility of retraction, staying firm on an opinion is not established. We will answer: The texts that indicate Ijma is hujjah do not differentiate between the death of the people of Ijma and their non-death. From this it is known that this has no bearing on Ijma being hujjah. And it is said that for later consensus, the absence of prior disagreement is a condition according to Abu Hanifa, i.e., when the mujtahids of a past era differed on a matter and then died, and then later scholars intend to make consensus on one of those sayings, it is said this Ijma is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. But this is not correct; rather it is correct that his opinion is that later consensus is valid, so that the previous disagreement is removed. Its parallel is the issue of selling Umm al-Walad. Because selling Umm al-Walad was not permissible according to Umar and permissible according to Ali. Then those after them made consensus that selling Umm al-Walad is not permissible. Therefore, if a judge gives a judgment allowing her sale, according to Imam Muhammad the judgment will not be enforced because it contradicts the later consensus. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling Umm al-Walad is permissible, according to one narration from al-Karkhi due to the previous disagreement. And in one narration, Imam Abu Yusuf is with him, and in another narration he is with Imam Muhammad.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, addresses the conditions required for the validity of Ijma (consensus) in Hanafi usul. The author systematically refutes several conditions proposed by other schools or individuals. First, the condition that the mujtahids must be from the Sahaba (Companions) or Ahl al-Bayt (household of the Prophet) is rejected. While these groups have virtue, their consensus is not exclusively hujjah; the consensus of any righteous mujtahids suffices. Second, the condition that they must be from Madinah (Imam Malik's view) is similarly refuted: the virtue of Madinans does not prove exclusivity. Third, Imam Shafi'i's condition of inqirad al-asr (extinction of the age) is dismissed because the proofs for Ijma do not differentiate between the mujtahids being alive or dead. Finally, the passage discusses a controversial point attributed to Abu Hanifa: that later consensus cannot override a previous disagreement. The author clarifies that the correct Hanafi position is that later consensus is valid and removes the earlier ikhtilaf. The example of selling Umm al-Walad illustrates this: Umar and Ali differed, then later scholars agreed that it is impermissible. Imam Muhammad holds that a judge's ruling allowing sale would be invalid due to the later consensus, while Abu Hanifa (in one riwaya) allows it due to the previous disagreement. The passage also addresses the condition of unanimity: the word 'ummah' in the hadith encompasses all, so even one dissenter prevents Ijma, contra the Mu'tazila who accept majority consensus.

Key Terms
انقراض العصر (inqirad al-asr): The passing away of all mujtahids of a given era

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the condition of inqirad al-asr for Ijma?
A) Because the possibility of retraction does not affect the validity of Ijma.
B) Because the textual proofs for Ijma do not differentiate between living and dead scholars.
C) Because Shafi'i's view is based on weak hadith.
D) Because mujtahids never retract their opinions.

Key Takeaway
Ijma is binding as soon as formed; the death of its participants is not a requirement for its authority.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
8 min
Later Consensus and the Principle of Unanimity in Ijma
Discussing later consensus and the requirement of unanimity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that later consensus (ijma' lahiq) overrides prior disagreement, and explain why unanimity is required for Ijma over majority consensus.

Core Idea
Later consensus removes earlier disagreement; unanimity is essential because truth may be with a single dissenter.

Two important issues in the theory of Ijma are addressed here: Can later scholars form a consensus that overrides a previous disagreement? And does Ijma require unanimity or is a majority sufficient? This lesson presents the Hanafi positions that later consensus is valid and that even one dissenter prevents Ijma.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem of later consensus
If earlier scholars differed on a matter and died, can later scholars form a consensus picking one of the previous views?
This is the issue of ijma' al-lahiqi.
2
State the correct Hanafi position
The correct view (as affirmed by the author) is that later consensus is valid and removes the earlier disagreement.
Countering an attribution to Abu Hanifa that he disallowed it.
3
Examine the Umm al-Walad example
Umar prohibited selling Umm al-Walad, Ali permitted it. Later scholars unanimously prohibited it. This illustrates the application.
The later consensus overrides the earlier ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the unanimity requirement
The hadith 'My community will not agree upon error' uses 'ummah' which includes all. Thus even one dissenter prevents Ijma.
Contrast with Mu'tazila who accept majority.
5
Refute the Mu'tazila proof
The hadith 'The Hand of Allah is with the group' is interpreted as applying after Ijma is formed, not at formation.
The group refers to those who adhere to consensus, not the majority.

اشرف الانوار شرح اردو ہوتی ہے اور جن امور میں ان پر تقلید واجب ہوتی ہے ان میں ان کے اختلاف کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ وكونه من الصحابة أو من العترة ولا يشترط اور اجماع کی اہمیت کے لئے صحابہ یا اہل بیت ہونا شرط نہیں یعنی بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اجتماع کے لئے صحابہ کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ بغیر صحابہ کے اجماع نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اسکی تعریف فرمائی ہے اور ان کے حق میں نیک خبر دی ہے۔ لہذا شرعی اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ میں نے تمھارے اندر ایسی چیز چھوڑی ہے کہ جب تک تم ان کو مضبوطی سے پکڑے رہو گے۔ ہر گز گمراہ نہ ہو گے ۔ اول کتاب اللہ دوسرے اہل بیت ہیں اور ہمارے نزدیک ان میں سے کوئی بھی شرط نہیں ہے۔ (یعنی نہ صحابی ہونا اور نہ اہل بیت رسول ہونا، نہ اہل قرابت رسول ہونا ) بلکہ اجماع کے لئے نیک صالح مجتہدین کا اجماع کافی ہے اور جو امور ان بعض لوگوں نے بیان کئے ہیں وہ ان کی ذاتی اور خاندانی فضیلت ہے۔ اس لئے نہیں کہ ان کا اجماع حجت ہے دوسروں کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے وكذا اهل المدينة او انقراض العصر الى طرح اہل مدینہ ہو یا زمانے کا ختم ہونا بھی شرط نہیں ہے یعنی اجماع کی اہمیت کے لئے مدینہ کا باشندہ ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ حضرت امام مالک رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اجتماع میں شرط ہے ان علماء کا اہل مدینہ ہونا شرط ہے اور دلیل یہ دیتے ہیں ان المدينة تنفى خبثها الخ۔ مدینہ گندگی اور میل کو اس ح پھینک دیتا ہے جس طرح بھٹی لوہے کے میل کو دور کر دیتی ہے اور اجتہاد میں خطاء کرنا بھی ایک میل ہے لہذا اہل مدینہ کا اجماع بے خطا ہو گا اور اس کا اختیار بھی کیا جائے گا۔ وَالْجَوَابُ أَنْ ذِأَلِكَ لَفَضلِهِمْ وَلَا يَكُونَ دَلِيْلاً عَلَىٰ أَنْ إِجْمَاعَهُمْ حُجَّةٌ لَا غَيْرَ وَقَالَ الشافَعِي يَسْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ اِنْقِراضَ الْعَصْرِ وَمَوْتُ جَمِيعِ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ تُوا عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ يُريدُ مَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ أَنْ يَجْمَعُوا عَلى قَوْلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهَا قِيلَ لَا يَجُوزُ ذالك الإجْمَاعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةٌ وَلَيْسَ كَذلِكَ فِى الصحيح بَلِ الصَّحِيحَ أَنَّهُ يَنْعَقِدُ عِنْدَهُ إِجْمَاعُ مُتَأَخِرُ وَيَرْتَفِعُ الخلاف السَّابِقُ مِنْ الْبَيْنِ وَنَظِيْرُهُ مَسألة بَيْع أم الوَلَدِ فَإِنَّهُ عِنْدَ لا يَجُوزُ وَعِنْدَ عَلِي يَجُوزُ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ أَجْمَعُوا عَلَىٰ عَدَمٍ جَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا فَإِنْ قضى الْقَاضِي بِجَوَازِ بَيْعِهَا لَا يَنْقَدْ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لِأَنَّهُ مُخَالِف لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق

نور الانوار جلد سوم

وَيَجُوزُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنَيْفَةَ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْكَرْخِي عَنْهُ لِأَهْلِ الْاِخْتِلَافِ السَّابِقِ وَأَبُويُوسُف فِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَهُ وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالشَّرْطُ إِجْمَاعُ الكُلِّ وَخِلافُ الْوَاحِدِ مَانِعَ خِلافِ الأكثر يَعْنِي فَى حِينِ انْعِقَادِ الإِجْمَاعِ لَوْ خَالَفَ وَاحِدٌ كَانَ خِلافُهُ معتبرًا وَلَا يَنْعَقِدُ الإجماع لأن لفظ الأُمَّةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لَا تَجْتَمِعُ أُمْتِي عَلى الصَّلَالَةِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الكُلِّ فَيَحْتَمِلُ أنْ يَكُونَ الصَّوابُ مَعَ مُخَالِف وَقَالَ بَعْضُ المُعْتَزِلَةِ يَنْعَقِدُ الإِجْمَاعُ بِاتِّفَاقِ الأكثرِ لأَنْ الْحَقِّ مَعَ الْجَمَاعَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السلام يَدُ اللهِ عَلَى الْجَمَاعَةِ فَمَنْ شَذَّ شَذَ فِي النَّارِ وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّ مَعْنَاهُ بَعْدَ تَحَقَّقِ الإِجْمَاعِ مَنْ شَذَّ وَخَرَجَ مَنْهُ دَخَلَ فِي النَّارِ. ترجمه تشریح والجواب : جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ اس سے اہل مدینہ کی فضیلت تو ثابت ہوتی ہے مگر اس سے لازم نہیں آتا کہ انہیں کا اجماع حجت غیر اہل مدینہ کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے ۔ فقال الشافعی رحمہ اللہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں۔ اجماع کے منعقد ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مجتہدین کا دور ختم ہو جائے اور مجتہدین باقی نہ ر ہیں وفات پا جائیں۔ لہذا جب تک وہ وفات نہ پائیں ان کا اجماع حجت نہیں ہے کیونکہ موت سے پہلے رجوع کا احتمال باقی رہتا ہے اور احتمال رجوع کے ہوتے ہوئے کسی رائے پر پر ترانہ رہنا ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ جواب ہم جواب دیں گے اجماع کے حجت ہونے پر جو نصوص دلالت کرتی ہیں۔ ان میں اہل اجماع کی موت اور تا عدم موت میں کوئی فرق وارد نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اجتماع کے حجت ہونے میں اس کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے ۔ وقِيلَ يُسْتَرَطُ لِلإجْمَاعِ اللاحق اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک زمانہ سابق میں اختلاف نہ ہونا شرط ہے بعد والوں کے اجماع کے ممبر ہونے کے لئے یعنی جب اهل ایک زمانے کے علاوہ مجتہدین کسی مسئلے میں اختلاف کریں اور پھر اس پر وفات پا جائیں پھر ان کے بعد علماء مجتہدین ارادہ کریں کہ ان کے کسی قول پر اجماع کر لیں تو کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ اجتماع امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ وليس كذالك في الصحیح۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی طرف اس قول کی نسبت ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ صحیح رائے حضرت امام صاحب کی یہ ہے کہ بعد والوں کا اجتماع درست ہے۔ تاکہ سابق اختلاف در میان سے دور ہو جائے اور اس کی نظیر ام ولد کی بیع کا مسئلہ ہے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کی بیع حضرت عمر کے نزدیک نا جائز اور حضرت علی کے نزدیک جائز ہے، پھر اس کے بعد والوں نے اس مسئلہ پر اجماع کیا کہ بیچ ام ولد کی جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اگر قاضی اس کے بیچ کا فیصلہ کر دے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ اجماع لاحق کے خلاف ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ام ولد کی بیع جائز ہے امام کرخی کی ایک روایت میں سابق اختلاف کی وجہ سے جائز ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں امام ابو یوسف بھی ان کے ساتھ ہیں اور ایک روایت میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں۔
Nur al-Anwar Volume 3. Ashraf al-Anwar is an Urdu commentary. In matters where taqlid upon them is obligatory, their disagreement is not considered. 'And that he be from the Companions or from the Ahl al-Bayt is not a condition.' For the importance of Ijma, being a Companion or Ahl al-Bayt is not a condition. Some said that for consensus, being a Companion is a condition; without Companions, no consensus. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) praised them and gave good news regarding them. Therefore they are the foundation for religious sciences and criticism and rulings. And some said consensus is not valid except only the consensus of the Ahl al-Bayt, i.e., his household and relatives, because the Prophet said: 'I have left among you something; as long as you hold fast to it, you will never go astray: first the Book of Allah, second my Ahl al-Bayt.' And according to us, none of these is a condition (i.e., neither being a Companion nor being of the Ahl al-Bayt nor being a relative). Rather, for Ijma, the consensus of righteous mujtahids is sufficient. And the matters that some people have mentioned are their personal and family virtue, not that their consensus is hujjah and others' consensus is not. Likewise, being from Madinah or the extinction of the age is also not a condition. That is, for the validity of Ijma, being a resident of Madinah is not a condition, as Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said that a condition for consensus is that the scholars be from Madinah. They give as proof: 'Madinah expels its impurities like the furnace removes the dross of iron.' Error in ijtihad is also an impurity, so the consensus of the people of Madinah will be infallible and must be followed. The answer: That is for their virtue, and it does not prove that their consensus is hujjah exclusively. And al-Shafi'i condition is the extinction of the age and the death of all mujtahids; their consensus is not hujjah until they die. And it is said that for later consensus, the absence of prior disagreement is a condition according to Abu Hanifa. That is, if the people of an era differed on a matter and then died, and then those after them intend to make consensus on one of those sayings, it is said this consensus is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. But this is not correct; rather the correct view is that later consensus is valid according to him and removes the previous disagreement. Its parallel is the issue of selling Umm al-Walad: it was not permissible according to Umar and permissible according to Ali. Then after that they made consensus that selling her is not permissible. So if a judge passes a judgment allowing her sale, according to Muhammad it is not executed because it contradicts the later consensus. And according to Abu Hanifa, in the narration of al-Karkhi from him, it is permissible due to the previous disagreement. And Abu Yusuf is with him in one narration, and with Muhammad in another. And the condition is the consensus of all, and the opposition of one prevents the opposition of the majority. That is, at the time of formation of Ijma, if one opposes, his opposition is considered, and Ijma is not formed because the word 'my community' in his saying (peace be upon him) 'My community will not agree upon error' encompasses all. So it is possible that the truth is with the opponent. And some Mu'tazila said that Ijma is formed by agreement of the majority because the truth is with the group, due to his saying: 'The Hand of Allah is with the group; whoever deviates, deviates into the Fire.' The answer: Its meaning is after Ijma is established, whoever deviates and leaves it enters the Fire. Translation/explanation: The answer to that is that it establishes the virtue of the people of Madinah, but it does not necessitate that their consensus alone is hujjah and others' is not. So al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The condition for the formation of Ijma is that the era of mujtahids ends and they die. Therefore, as long as they are alive, their consensus is not hujjah because before death there remains the possibility of retraction, and with the possibility of retraction, staying firm on an opinion is not established. We will answer: The texts that indicate Ijma is hujjah do not differentiate between the death of the people of Ijma and their non-death. From this it is known that this has no bearing on Ijma being hujjah. And it is said that for later consensus, the absence of prior disagreement is a condition according to Abu Hanifa, i.e., when the mujtahids of a past era differed on a matter and then died, and then later scholars intend to make consensus on one of those sayings, it is said this Ijma is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. But this is not correct; rather it is correct that his opinion is that later consensus is valid, so that the previous disagreement is removed. Its parallel is the issue of selling Umm al-Walad. Because selling Umm al-Walad was not permissible according to Umar and permissible according to Ali. Then those after them made consensus that selling Umm al-Walad is not permissible. Therefore, if a judge gives a judgment allowing her sale, according to Imam Muhammad the judgment will not be enforced because it contradicts the later consensus. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling Umm al-Walad is permissible, according to one narration from al-Karkhi due to the previous disagreement. And in one narration, Imam Abu Yusuf is with him, and in another narration he is with Imam Muhammad.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, addresses the conditions required for the validity of Ijma (consensus) in Hanafi usul. The author systematically refutes several conditions proposed by other schools or individuals. First, the condition that the mujtahids must be from the Sahaba (Companions) or Ahl al-Bayt (household of the Prophet) is rejected. While these groups have virtue, their consensus is not exclusively hujjah; the consensus of any righteous mujtahids suffices. Second, the condition that they must be from Madinah (Imam Malik's view) is similarly refuted: the virtue of Madinans does not prove exclusivity. Third, Imam Shafi'i's condition of inqirad al-asr (extinction of the age) is dismissed because the proofs for Ijma do not differentiate between the mujtahids being alive or dead. Finally, the passage discusses a controversial point attributed to Abu Hanifa: that later consensus cannot override a previous disagreement. The author clarifies that the correct Hanafi position is that later consensus is valid and removes the earlier ikhtilaf. The example of selling Umm al-Walad illustrates this: Umar and Ali differed, then later scholars agreed that it is impermissible. Imam Muhammad holds that a judge's ruling allowing sale would be invalid due to the later consensus, while Abu Hanifa (in one riwaya) allows it due to the previous disagreement. The passage also addresses the condition of unanimity: the word 'ummah' in the hadith encompasses all, so even one dissenter prevents Ijma, contra the Mu'tazila who accept majority consensus.

Key Terms
إجماع اللاحق (ijma' al-lahiqi): Later consensus formed after a previous era of disagreement
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who gives birth to her master's child

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum requirement for the number of mujtahids whose agreement constitutes Ijma?
A) Majority is sufficient.
B) Two are enough.
C) All mujtahids must agree; even one dissenter prevents Ijma.
D) It depends on the region.

Key Takeaway
Later consensus overrides earlier disagreement, and unanimity is essential because the guarantee of infallibility only applies when all mujtahids agree.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Condition of Unanimity for Ijma
Discussion of condition that Ijma requires unanimity of all mujtahids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires unanimity of all mujtahids for the formation of Ijma and evaluate the Mu'tazila argument for majority consensus.

Core Idea
Ijma requires unanimity; a single dissenter prevents consensus because truth may be with the dissenter.

In this passage from Sharh Nur al-Anwar, the author establishes a fundamental usul rule: Ijma (consensus) is only valid when every mujtahid in that era agrees. Even a single dissenter blocks Ijma. The proof is the hadith 'My ummah does not gather upon misguidance' – the word 'ummati' includes all, so the dissenter could be correct. The author then refutes the Mu'tazila who argue that majority agreement suffices, showing that the hadith they cite applies only after actual consensus, not before.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly that Ijma requires the unanimous agreement of all mujtahids. Note that disagreement of one is an impediment just like disagreement of the majority.
The key phrase: 'والشّرط إجماع الكلّ'.
2
Examine the primary dalil
Analyze the hadith 'لا تجتمع أمتي على الضلالة'. The word 'أمتي' is a general term ('amm) that includes all mujtahids. According to Hanafi usul, a general command indicates obligation, and here it implies that if all agree, they cannot be on error; thus, if even one dissents, the possibility of him being correct prevents Ijma.
This dalil is zanni al-thubut (ahad) but qat'i al-dalala for the concept.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
The Mu'tazila claim that majority agreement suffices, citing 'يد الله على الجماعة'. They interpret 'al-jama'ah' as the majority.
Their hadith appears to support group consensus.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes the timing: the hadith about the hand of Allah being with the group applies after Ijma is actually formed. So it does not justify forming Ijma by majority alone; it warns against leaving an already established consensus.
The response uses ta'wil (interpretation) to harmonize the proofs.
5
Note additional conditions (Shafi'i and prior disagreement)
The passage also mentions the Shafi'i condition that mujtahids must have died for Ijma to be binding (to prevent retraction), and an opinion attributed to Abu Hanifa that prior disagreement blocks later Ijma. The Hanafi response rejects both, affirming that texts do not differentiate life/death and that later Ijma can override prior ikhtilaf.
Example: the sale of umm walad.

وَيَجُوْدُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنَيْفَةَ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْكَرْخِي عَنْهُ لَأَهْلِ الْاِخْتِلَافِ السَّابِقِ وَأَبُويُوسُف فِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَهُ وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ مَعَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالشَّرْطُ إِجْمَاعُ الكُلِّ وَخِلافُ الْوَاحِدِ مَانِعَ خِلافِ الأكثر يَعْنِي فَى جِيْنِ انْعِقَادِ الإِجْمَاعِ لَوْ خَالَفَ وَاحِدٌ كَانَ خِلافُهُ معتبرًا وَلَا يَنْعَقِدُ الإجماع لأن لفظ الأُمَّةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ صحیح رائے حضرت امام صاحب کی یہ ہے کہ بعد والوں کا اجتماع درست ہے۔ تاکہ سابق اختلاف در میان سے دور ہو جائے اور اس کی نظیر امتہ والد کی بیع کا مسئلہ ہے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کی بیع حضرت عمر کے نزدیک نا جائز اور حضرت علی کے نزدیک جائز ہے، پھر اس کے بعد والوں نے اس مسئلہ پر اجماع کیا کہ بیچ ام ولد کی جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اگر قاضی اس کے بیچ کا فیصلہ کر دے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ اجماع لاحق کے خلاف ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ام ولد کی بیع جائز ہے امام کرخی کی ایک روایت میں سابق اختلاف کی وجہ ۔ اور ایک روایت میں امام ابو یوسف بھی ان کے ساتھ ہیں اور ایک روایت میں امام محمد کے ساتھ ہیں۔
وَالشَّرْطُ إِجْمَاعُ الكُل وخلاف الواحد الج اور اجماع منعقد ہونے کے لئے تمام اہل اجتماع کا اتفاق شرط ہے۔ کسی ایک کا اختلاف بھی اجماع سے مانع ہے۔ جس طرح اکثریت کا اختلاف مانع ہے۔ یعنی اجماع کے منعقد ہونے کے وقت اگر کسی ایک نے اختلاف کر دیا تو اس کا اختلاف معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اجماع منعقد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ "امتہ " جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے فرمان "لاتجتمع أمتي على الضلالة" میری امت گمراہی پر جمع نہ ہو گی۔ میں اجماع کل کو شامل ہے اس لئے کہ احتمال ہے کہ صواب مخالفت کرنے والے کے ساتھ ہو اور بعض معتزلہ نے کہا ہے کہ اکثر کے اتفاق کر لینے سے اجماع منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حق ہمیشہ جماعت کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے- "يد الله على الجماعة، من شذ شذ في النار" (اللہ تعالی کی چیدہ جماعت کے ساتھ ہے۔ جو جماعت سے بعد ہو جائے وہ اکیلا جہنم میں جائے گا) والجواب ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ اجتماع متحقق ہو جانے کے بعد جو شخص جماعت سے اختلاف کرے اور نکل جائے وہ شخص جہنم میں جائے گا۔
It is valid according to Abu Hanifa in the narration of al-Karkhi from him regarding the prior disagreement, and Abu Yusuf in one narration with him, and in one narration with Muhammad. The condition is consensus of all, and the disagreement of one is an impediment just as disagreement of the majority. That is, at the time of formation of Ijma, if one disagrees, his disagreement is considered and Ijma is not formed, because the word 'ummati' in his statement (peace be upon him) 'My ummah does not gather upon misguidance' includes all, so it is possible that the truth is with the dissenter. Some Mu'tazila said Ijma is formed by agreement of the majority, because the truth is with the group, due to his statement (peace be upon him) 'The hand of Allah is with the group, whoever deviates deviates into the Fire.' The response is that its meaning is after the actualization of Ijma, whoever deviates and leaves it enters the Fire. Translation explanation and response: The response to this is that it proves the virtue of the people of Medina, but it does not necessitate that only their Ijma is proof and the Ijma of non-Medinans is not proof. Then al-Shafi'i said: The condition for Ijma is that the era of the mujtahids ends and they die. So as long as they have not died, their Ijma is not proof because before death there remains the possibility of retraction, and with the possibility of retraction, remaining upon an opinion is not established. Response: We reply that the texts that indicate the proof of Ijma do not differentiate between the death of the people of Ijma and their non-death. So it is understood that this has no bearing on the proof of Ijma. And it was said: The condition is required for Ijma... and some people said that according to Abu Hanifa, the absence of prior disagreement is a condition for the later Ijma to be valid. But that is not correct in the sahih. Rather, the correct view of Imam Abu Hanifa is that later Ijma is valid, so that prior disagreement is removed. An example is the sale of umm walad. Because the sale of umm walad is impermissible according to Umar and permissible according to Ali, then later scholars formed Ijma that the sale of umm walad is not permissible. So if a judge gives a ruling on its sale, according to Imam Muhammad the ruling is not executed because this Ijma is against the later [ijma]. And according to Abu Hanifa, the sale of umm walad is permissible. In one narration of al-Karkhi due to prior disagreement, and in one narration Abu Yusuf is with him, and in one narration he is with Muhammad. And the condition is consensus of all and disagreement of one... and for Ijma to be formed, agreement of all the people of assembly is a condition. The disagreement of a single person prevents Ijma, just as disagreement of the majority does. That is, at the time of formation of Ijma if one disagrees, his disagreement is considered and Ijma will not form. Because the word 'ummah' in the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'My ummah does not gather upon misguidance' includes all, because it is possible that the truth is with the dissenter. And some Mu'tazila said that Ijma is formed by the agreement of the majority, because the truth is always with the group. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The hand of Allah is with the group; whoever deviates deviates into the Fire.' Our response is that after Ijma is actualized, whoever disagrees with the group and leaves it will enter the Fire.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul rule regarding the condition for the validity of Ijma (consensus). The author, commenting on the matn of Nur al-Anwar, emphasizes that Ijma requires the unanimous agreement of all mujtahids; even a single dissenter prevents the formation of Ijma. The proof is the famous hadith 'La tajtami' ummati 'ala al-dalal' (My ummah will not gather upon misguidance), which includes all members of the ummah. The possibility that the dissenter holds the truth cannot be ruled out. The Mu'tazila argue that majority agreement suffices, citing the hadith 'Yad Allah ma'a al-jama'ah' (The hand of Allah is with the group). The Hanafi response clarifies that this hadith applies after the actual formation of Ijma, not before. The passage also addresses the Shafi'i condition that the mujtahids must have died for Ijma to be valid; the Hanafi response is that the textual proofs for Ijma do not differentiate between life and death. Additionally, the text refutes an opinion attributed to Abu Hanifa that prior disagreement among earlier scholars prevents later Ijma, stating that the correct view is that later Ijma can override prior disagreement, as exemplified by the case of selling an umm walad.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of all mujtahids of the ummah after the Prophet on a religious ruling.
المخالف (al-mukhalif): A mujtahid who dissents from the majority or from a potential consensus.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): The group, here referring to the body of mujtahids who have formed Ijma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, when does the hadith 'يد الله على الجماعة' apply?
A) Before the formation of Ijma
B) After Ijma is actualized
C) Only to the scholars of Medina
D) It is not a valid hadith

Key Takeaway
Ijma requires the unanimous agreement of all mujtahids; a single dissenter prevents consensus because truth may be with the dissenter.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
6 min
Ijma Yields Certainty: Quranic Proofs and Refutation of Deniers
Explanation that Ijma yields certainty with Quranic proofs and refutation of deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that Ijma in principle yields definitive certainty (qat'iyyah), cite the three Quranic proofs for its authority, and evaluate the argument that Ijma requires a prior cause (da'i).

Core Idea
Ijma in principle gives yaqin (certainty); rejecting a definitive Ijma renders one a disbeliever.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar establishes the ruling of Ijma in Usul al-Fiqh: it yields certainty in legal matters. It provides three Quranic verses that prove the authority of consensus, refutes those who deny Ijma entirely, and discusses an internal debate over whether a prior speculative proof is necessary for its formation. The preferred Hanafi view is that a cause (da'i) is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling of Ijma in principle
The text states that Ijma yields yaqin and qat'iyyah. Understand that this is the default ruling (al-asl).
Exceptions like sukuti Ijma do not remove the principle.
2
Analyze the three Quranic proofs for Ijma
The author cites verses 2:143, 3:110, and 4:115. For each, identify the operative phrase and how it establishes the authority of consensus.
The verses describe the ummah as just, best, and equate following their way with following the Messenger.
3
Examine the refutation of the deniers
The Mu'tazila and Rafida argue that individuals can err, so the whole group can err. The author rebuts by analogizing to a mountain of sand particles – the collective strength prevents error.
This refutation affirms the qat'iyyah of Ijma against philosophical skepticism.
4
Evaluate the condition of a prior cause (da'i)
Scholars differed on whether Ijma requires a prior speculative proof (dalil zanni) or can occur spontaneously. The author endorses the view that a cause is necessary.
This condition ensures Ijma is grounded in evidence, not mere coincidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَحُكْمُهُ فِي الأصْلِ أَنْ يَثْبُتَ الْعَرَادُ به شرْعًا عَلى سَبِيلِ الْيَقِينِ يَعْنِي أَنْ الإِجْمَاعَ فِي الْأَمُورِ الشَّرَيْعَةِ فِي الأَصْلِ يُفِيدُ الْيَقِينَ وَالْقَطْعِيةَ فَيُكَفِّرُ جَاجِدَة وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ الْمَوَاضِع بسب الْعَارض لا يُفِيدُ القَطعَ كَالإجماع السكوتي بِسَبَ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَكَذَالِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطًا لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ وَصَفَهُمْ بالواسطية وَفِي العَادِلَةُ فَيَكُونُ إِجْمَاعَهُمْ حَجَّةً وَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمة أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ وَالْخَيْرِيةُ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بِاعْتِبَارِ كَمَالِهِمْ فَيَكُونُ إِجْمَاعُهُمْ حُجَّةً وَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى وَمَنْ يُشاقِقِ الرَّسُوْلَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيْنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرُ سبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِيْنَ نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى فَجُعِلَتْ مُخَالَفَهُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِثْلَ مُخَالَفَةِ الرَّسُولِ فيَكُونُ اِجمَاعَهُمْ كَخَيْرِ الرَّسُولِ حُجَّةٌ قَطْعِيةٌ وَامْثَالُهُ وَقَدْ ضَلَّ بَعْضُ الْمَعْتَزِلَة وَالروافض فَقَالُوا إِنَّ الإِجْمَاعَ لَيْسَ بِحُجْةٍ لأَنْ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُخْطِئًا فَكَذَا الْجَمِيْعُ وَلَا يَدْرُونَ قُوةَ الْجَبَلِ المُؤلّفِ مِنَ الشَّعْرَاتِ وَأَمْثَالِهِ ثُمَّ إِنَّهُمْ اِخْتَلَفُوا فِي أَن الأَجْمَاعَ هَلْ يَسْتَرِطُ فِى اِنْعِقَادِهِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ دَاعٍ مُقَدِّم عَلَيْهِ مِنْ دَلَيْلٍ ظَنِّي أَوْ يَنْعَقِدُ فَجَاءَةٌ بِلادَلِيْلٍ بَاعِثِ عَلَيْهِ بِالْهَامِ وَتَوْفِيقِ مِن الله بأن يَخلُقَ اللهُ فِيهِ عِلْمَاءُ ضَرُودِيًا وَيُوَفَّقَهُمُ الاخْتِيَارِ الصَّوَابِ فَقِيْلَ لاَ يَسْتَرِطُ لَهُ الدَّاعِى وَالأَصْحُ الْمُخْتَارُ أنَّه لابُدَّلَهُ مِنْ دَاعٍ عَلَى مَا قَالَ المُصنف
And its ruling in principle is that it establishes the intent legally upon certainty, meaning that Ijma in religious matters in principle yields certainty and definitiveness, so it renders the denier a disbeliever. Although in some places due to an obstacle it does not yield certainty, like sukuti Ijma. Because of His statement (ta'ala): 'Thus We have made you a middle nation that you may be witnesses over the people' (2:143) – He described them as middle and just, so their Ijma is proof. And also His statement: 'You are the best nation produced for mankind' (3:110) – goodness is by virtue of their completeness, so their Ijma is proof. And also His statement: 'And whoever contradicts the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the way of the believers – We will give him what he has taken' (4:115) – thus opposing the believers is made like opposing the Messenger, so their Ijma like the word of the Messenger is a definitive proof. And similar verses. Some Mu'tazila and Rafida have deviated, saying Ijma is not a proof because each individual may err, so likewise the entire group. They do not know the strength of a mountain composed of sand particles and the like. Then they differed on whether Ijma in its formation requires a prior cause from a speculative proof (dalil zanni) or whether it is formed suddenly without a proof, by divine inspiration and guidance from Allah, by Allah creating necessary knowledge in them and directing them to choose the correct opinion. It was said that it does not require a cause. The most correct and chosen view is that it must have a cause, as the author said.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage explains the authoritative nature of Ijma. In principle, Ijma provides yaqin (certainty) and qat'iyyah (definitiveness) in legal matters, to the extent that rejecting a definitive Ijma renders one a disbeliever (takfir). However, due to certain obstacles, not every type of Ijma yields such certainty; for example, sukuti Ijma (where some remain silent) does not produce certainty. The Quranic proofs cited include three verses: (1) 'Ja'alnakum ummatan wasata' (2:143) – describing the ummah as just, so their consensus is a proof; (2) 'Kuntum khayra ummatin' (3:110) – their goodness implies their consensus is correct; (3) 'Wa man yushaqiqi al-rasula... wa yattabi' ghayra sabil al-mu'minin' (4:115) – equating opposing the believers with opposing the Messenger, thus their way (consensus) is decisive. The text then refutes the Mu'tazila and Rafida who deny Ijma on the grounds that individuals may err, arguing that the collective agreement of many cannot be erroneous, like a mountain of sand particles. Finally, the passage presents a debate on whether Ijma requires a prior speculative proof (dalil zanni) or can occur spontaneously by divine guidance. The preferred view is that a cause (da'i) in the form of a prior proof is necessary.

Key Terms
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty; Ijma yields yaqin in legal rulings in principle.
الإجماع السكوتي (al-ijma' al-sukuti): Consensus where some mujtahids remain silent without explicitly agreeing.
الداعي (al-da'i): A prior proof or cause that prompts the formation of Ijma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Ijma in principle?
A) It provides only speculative (zanni) knowledge
B) It provides certainty (yaqin) and definitiveness (qat'iyyah)
C) It is not a valid proof in Islam
D) It requires the death of all mujtahids

Key Takeaway
Ijma in principle yields definitive certainty; its proof is from Quran and its denier becomes a disbeliever.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
10 min
Ijma: Unanimity, Certainty, and the Need for a Prior Dalil
Explains conditions for ijma, its certainty, and the requirement of a prior speculative evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for valid ijma according to the Hanafi school, explain its definitive evidentiary value, and apply the school's requirement of a prior speculative evidence (da'i) to evaluate a claimed ijma.

Core Idea
Ijmāʿ is the definitive consensus of all mujtahids, requires a prior speculative proof to motivate agreement, and denying it is disbelief.

This lesson explores the Hanafi conditions for valid ijma (consensus), its epistemological weight as a source of certainty, and the crucial requirement that ijma must be preceded by a speculative evidence (da'i) that impels scholars to agree. We will examine the scriptural proofs for ijma's authority, the refutation of those who reject it, and the internal dispute on whether a prior dalil is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition for Ijma
The passage states that ijma requires the agreement of all scholars (ahl al-ijma'); the dissent of even one prevents its formation. This is based on the hadith 'My ummah does not agree upon error' and the possibility that truth may lie with the dissenter. Note the Mu'tazila counter-argument and its Hanafi refutation.
The hadith 'The hand of Allah is with the group' is interpreted as applying after consensus is established, not before.
2
Recognize the Epistemic Status of Ijma
Ijma yields certainty (yakin) and definitiveness (qat') in principle, so denying a ruling proven by definitive ijma is disbelief. However, some forms (e.g., silent consensus) may not reach certainty due to external impediments.
Silent consensus (ijma sukuti) is when some scholars remain silent after others express an opinion; it is considered a weaker type.
3
Locate the Quranic Proofs
The passage cites three verses: Qur'an 2:143 (middle nation as just witnesses), 3:110 (best nation), and 4:115 (opposing believers like opposing the Messenger). Explain how each verse establishes collective infallibility and makes ijma a definitive proof (hujja qat'iyya).
The verse 4:115 equates following a path other than the believers' with contradicting the Messenger, giving ijma the same binding force as a definitive proof.
4
Analyze the Dispute on Necessity of Da'i
The passage presents a dispute: some scholars allow ijma to be formed spontaneously through divine inspiration, while the Hanafi school (and the author) require a prior speculative evidence (da'i) like khabar wahid or qiyas. The relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) is that a da'i is necessary.
The example of selling food before taking possession illustrates: the ijma on its prohibition was motivated by the Prophetic hadith. Without such a da'i, the consensus would not be valid.

Source Text

وَالشَّرْطُ إِجْمَاعُ الكُل وخلاف الواحد [الج؟]. اور اجماع منعقد ہونے کے لئے تمام اہل اجتماع کا اتفاق شرط ہے۔ کسی ایک کا اختلاف بھی اجماع سے مانع ہے۔ جس طرح اکثریت کا اختلاف مانع ہے۔ یعنی اجماع کے منعقد ہونے کے وقت اگر کسی ایک نے اختلاف کر دیا تو اس کا اختلاف معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اجماع منعقد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ "امتہ" جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے فرمان "لاتَجْمَعُ أُمَّتِي عَلَى الضَّلَالَةِ" میری امت گمراہی پر جمع نہ ہو گی۔ میں اجماع کل کو شامل ہے اس لئے کہ احتمال ہے کہ صواب مخالفت کرنے والے کے ساتھ ہو اور بعض معتزلہ نے کہا ہے کہ اکثر کے اتفاق کر لینے سے اجماع منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حق ہمیشہ جماعت کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے- يَدُ اللَّهِ عَلَى الْجَمَاعَةِ مَنْ شَذَّ شَذَّ فِي النَّارِ) اللہ تعالی کی چیدہ جماعت کے ساتھ ہے۔ جو جماعت سے بعد ہو جائے وہ اکیلا جہنم میں جائے گا) والجواب ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ اجتماع متحقق ہو جانے کے بعد جو شخص جماعت سے اختلاف کرے اور نکل جائے وہ شخص جہنم میں جائے گا۔
وَحُكْمُهُ فِي الأصْلِ أَنْ يَثْبُتَ الْعَرَادُ به شرْعًا عَلى سَبِيلِ الْيَقِينِ يَعْنِي أَنْ الإِجْمَاعَ فِي الْأَمُورِ الشَّرَيْعَةِ فِي الأَصْلِ يُفِيدُ الْيَقِينَ وَالْقَطْعِيةَ فَيُكَفِّرُ جَاجِدَة وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ الْمَوَاضِع بسب الْعَارض لا يُفِيدُ القَطعَ كَالإجماع السكوتي بِسَبَ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَكَذَالِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطًا لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ وَصَفَهُمْ بالواسطية وَفِي العَادِلَةُ فَيَكُونُ إِجْمَاعَهُمْ حَجَّةً وَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمة أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ وَالْخَيْرِيةُ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بِاعْتِبَارِ كَمَالِهِمْ فَيَكُونُ إِجْمَاعُهُمْ حُجَّةً وَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى وَمَنْ يُشاقِقِ الرَّسُوْلَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيْنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرُ سبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِيْنَ نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى فَجُعِلَتْ مُخَالَفَهُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِثْلَ مُخَالَفَةِ الرَّسُولِ فيَكُونُ اِجمَاعَهُمْ كَخَيْرِ الرَّسُولِ حُجَّةٌ قَطْعِيةٌ وَامْثَالُهُ وَقَدْ ضَلَّ بَعْضُ الْمَعْتَزِلَة وَالروافض فَقَالُوا إِنَّ الإِجْمَاعَ لَيْسَ بِحُجْةٍ لأَنْ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُخْطِئًا فَكَذَا الْجَمِيْعُ وَلَا يَدْرُونَ قُوةَ الْجَبَلِ المُؤلّفِ مِنَ الشَّعْرَاتِ وَأَمْثَالِهِ ثُمَّ إِنَّهُمْ اِخْتَلَفُوا فِي أَن الأَجْمَاعَ هَلْ يَسْتَرِطُ فِى اِنْعِقَادِهِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ دَاعٍ مُقَدِّم عَلَيْهِ مِنْ دَلَيْلٍ ظَنِّي أَوْ يَنْعَقِدُ فَجَاءَةٌ بِلادَلِيْلٍ بَاعِثِ عَلَيْهِ بِالْهَامِ وَتَوْفِيقِ مِن الله بأن يَخلُقَ اللهُ فِيهِ عِلْمَاءُ ضَرُودِيًا وَيُوَفَّقَهُمُ الاخْتِيَارِ الصَّوَابِ فَقِيْلَ لاَ يَسْتَرِطُ لَهُ الدَّاعِى وَالأَصْحُ الْمُخْتَارُ أنَّه لابُدَّلَهُ مِنْ دَاعٍ عَلَى مَا قَالَ المُصنف
And the condition is consensus of all, and the opposition of one [؟]. For the ijma to be concluded, agreement of all people of assembly is a condition. The disagreement of a single person also prevents ijma. Just as the disagreement of a majority prevents it. That is, at the time of the conclusion of ijma, if one person dissents, his dissent will be considered valid, and ijma will not be concluded. Because the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'My ummah does not agree upon error.' It includes the entire ummah, because it is possible that the truth is with the dissenter. And some Mu'tazila said that ijma is concluded with the agreement of the majority, because truth is always with the group. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The hand of Allah is with the group; whoever deviates, deviates to the Fire.' The answer from our side is that after the consensus has been established, the person who dissents and leaves the group will go to the Fire. And its ruling in principle is that the intent of the Law is established with certainty, meaning that ijma in legal matters in principle yields certainty and definitiveness, so its denier is considered a disbeliever. But in some places due to an impediment it does not yield certainty, like silent consensus. Because of His statement: 'Thus We have made you a middle nation that you may be witnesses over mankind.' He described them as middle (just), so their consensus is a proof. Also His statement: 'You are the best nation brought forth for mankind.' Goodness is due to their perfection, so their consensus is a proof. Also His statement: 'And whoever contradicts the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows a way other than that of the believers, We will turn him to what he has turned to.' So opposing the believers is made like opposing the Messenger, thus their consensus is like the report of the Messenger, a definitive proof. And similar proofs. And some Mu'tazila and Rawafid deviated and said that ijma is not a proof because each of them may be mistaken, so likewise the entire group may be mistaken. They do not know the strength of a rope made of many strands. Then they disagreed among themselves whether ijma requires a prior motive from a speculative proof, or whether it can be concluded suddenly without a motivating proof by divine inspiration and guidance, such that Allah creates in them necessary knowledge and grants them success in choosing the correct view. Some said that a motive is not required, but the sound chosen view is that a motive is necessary, as the author said.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage deals with the conditions and evidentiary value of ijma (consensus) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first states that ijma requires the agreement of all scholars (ahl al-hall wa al-aqd); the dissent of even a single individual prevents the formation of ijma. This is based on the hadith 'My ummah does not agree upon error,' which implies that if there is a dissenter, the consensus of the rest is not a guarantee of correctness, as truth may lie with the dissenter. The Mu'tazila are reported to have held that majority agreement suffices, citing the hadith 'The hand of Allah is with the group.' However, the Hanafi response clarifies that the hadith refers to those who leave the group after consensus has been established, not to the initial dissenter.

Next, the passage explains the epistemological weight of ijma: in principle (fi al-asl), ijma yields certainty (yakin) and definitiveness (qat'iyya), so that denying a ruling proven by definitive ijma amounts to disbelief (takfir). However, in some cases, such as silent consensus (ijma sukuti), it may not yield certainty due to an external impediment.

Then the passage provides scriptural proofs for the authority of ijma: Quranic verses (2:143, 3:110, 4:115) that establish the ummah as just, best, and make opposing them equivalent to opposing the Messenger. These indicate that their consensus is a definitive proof (hujja qat'iyya).

The passage refutes those (some Mu'tazila and Rawafid) who reject ijma altogether, arguing that the possibility of error in individuals does not negate the collective infallibility, using the analogy of a rope made of many strands.

Finally, the passage presents a dispute among those who accept ijma: whether its formation requires a prior speculative evidence (dalil zanni) as a motive (da'i), such as a khabar wahid or qiyas, or whether it can be formed spontaneously through divine inspiration. The author (the matn of Nur al-Anwar) affirms the sound view (al-asahh al-mukhtar) that a prior motive is necessary. The subsequent part of the text (on the next page) gives examples: their consensus on the invalidity of selling food before taking possession was motivated by the Prophet's hadith.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of qualified scholars (mujtahids) of the Muslim community on a legal ruling after the death of the Prophet.
داعٍ (da'in): A motive or prior evidence (usually a speculative proof like khabar wahid or qiyas) that impels the mujtahids to agree on a particular ruling, necessary for the formation of valid ijma.
أخبار الآحاد (akhbar al-ahad): Solitary hadith reports that do not reach the level of tawatur, considered speculative (zanni) in proof, but can serve as a da'i for ijma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon (mukhtar) view regarding a prior evidence (da'i) for the formation of ijma?
A) No prior evidence is required; ijma can be formed by divine inspiration alone.
B) A prior speculative evidence (like khabar wahid or qiyas) is necessary.
C) A prior definitive evidence (like mutawatir Hadith) is required.
D) The prior evidence must be from the Quran only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the unanimous agreement of all qualified scholars for ijma, which yields definitive certainty in principle, and necessitates a prior speculative evidence (da'i) to motivate the consensus.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
